
**[]()Bhāvanā:** 'mental development' lit. 'calling into existence, producing' is what in English is generally but rather vaguely called 'meditation'. One has to distinguish 2 kinds: development of tranquillity [*samatha\-bhāvanā*](dic3_s.htm#samatha-bhāvanā), i.e. concentration [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi), and development of insight *[vipassanā](dic3_v.htm#vipassanā)* \- *[bhāvanā](dic3_b.htm#bhāvanā),* i.e. understanding *[paññā](dic3_p.htm#paññā).*

These two important terms, tranquillity and insight see: [*samatha\-vipassanā*](dic3_s.htm#samatha-vipassanā), are very often met with and explained in the Sutta, as well as in the Abhidhamma.

Tranquillity [*samatha*](dic3_s.htm#samatha) is the concentrated, unshaken, peaceful, and therefore undefiled state of mind, whilst insight [*vipassanā*](dic3_v.htm#vipassanā) is the intuitive insight into the [impermanence](dic3_a.htm#anicca), [misery](dic3_d.htm#dukkha) and [impersonality](dic3_a.htm#anattā) [*anicca*](dic3_a.htm#anicca) [*dukkha*](dic3_d.htm#dukkha) [*anattā*](dic3_a.htm#anattā) see: [*tilakkhana*](dic3_t.htm#tilakkhana) of all bodily and mental phenomena of existence, included in the 5 groups of existence, namely, materiality, feeling, perception, mental constructions and consciousness; see: [*khandha*](dic3_k.htm#khandha).

Tranquillity, or concentration of mind, according to Sankhepavannana Commentary to Abhidhammattha\-sangaha, bestows a threefold blessing: favourable rebirth, present happy life, and purity of mind which is the condition of insight. Concentration [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) is the indispensable foundation and precondition of insight by purifying the mind from the 5 mental defilements or hindrances [*nīvarana*](dic3_n.htm#nīvarana), whilst insight [*vipassanā*](dic3_v.htm#vipassanā) produces the 4 supra mundane stages of Nobility and deliverance of mind. The [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) therefore says: May you develop mental concentration, o Bhikkhus; for who is mentally concentrated, sees things according to reality see: XXII, 5. And in [Mil.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Mil.) it is said: Just as when a lighted lamp is brought into a dark chamber, the lamp\-light Will destroy the darkness and produce and spread the light, just so will insight, once arisen, destroy the darkness of ignorance and produce the light of knowledge.

[Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) III\-XI gives full directions how to attain full concentration and the absorptions [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna) by means of the following 40 meditation subjects [*kammatthāna*](dic3_k.htm#kammatthāna):

>
>
>
>
> 10 kasina\-exercises see: [*kasina*](dic3_k.htm#kasina). These produce the 4 absorptions
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 10 loathsome subjects [*asubha*](dic3_a.htm#asubha). These produce the 1st absorption.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 10 recollections [*anussati*](dic3_a.htm#anussati): of the [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) [*buddhānussati*](dic3_b.htm#buddhānussati), the Doctrine [*dhammānussati*](dic3_d.htm#dhammānussati), the Brotherhood of the Noble Ones [*sanghānussati*](dic3_s.htm#sanghānussati), morality, generosity, the divine beings, death [*maranasati*](dic3_m.htm#maranasati), the body [*kāyagatāsati*](dic3_k.htm#kāyagatāsati),, in\-and\-outbreathing [*ānāpāna\-sati*](dic3_a.htm#ānāpāna-sati) and peace [*upasamānussati*](dic3_u.htm#upasamānussati),. Among these, the recollection or awareness or mindfulness of in\-and\-out breathing may produce all the 4 absorptions, that of the body the 1st absorption, the rest only neighbourhood\-concentration [*upacāra\-samādhi*](dic3_u.htm#upacāra-samādhi), see: [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi).
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 4 sublime abodes [*brahma\-vihāra*](dic3_b.htm#brahma-vihāra): loving\-kindness, Pity, altruistic joy, equanimity *[mettā](dic3_m.htm#mettā),* [*karunā*](dic3_k.htm#karunā), *[muditā](dic3_m.htm#muditā),* *[upekkhā](dic3_u.htm#upekkhā).* Of these, the first 3 exercises may produce 3 absorptions, the last one the 4th absorption only.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 4 immaterial spheres *arūpāyatana* see. [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna): of unbounded space, unbounded consciousness, nothingness, neither\-perception\-nor\-non\-perception. These are based upon the 4th absorption.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 1 perception of the loathsomeness of food [*āhāre patikkūla\-saññā*](dic3_a.htm#āhāre%20patikkūla-saññā), which may produce neighbourhood\-concentration
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 1 analysis of the 4 elements *catudhātu* \- [*vavatthāna*](dic3_v.htm#vavatthāna) see. [*dhātu\-vavatthāna*](dic3_d.htm#dhātu-vavatthāna), which may produce neighbourhood\-concentration.
>
>
>
>

Mental development forms one of the 3 kinds of meritorious action [*puñña\-kiriya\-vatthu*](dic3_p.htm#puñña-kiriya-vatthu). 'Delight in meditation' *[bhāvanā](dic3_b.htm#bhāvanā)* \- *rāmatā* is one of the noble usages [*ariya\-vamsa*](dic3_a.htm#ariya-vamsa).

**[[birth process]]Birth process:** [*upapatti\-bhava*](dic3_u.htm#upapatti-bhava): see: [*bhava*](dic3_b.htm#bhava). Further see: *patisandhi, jāti*

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "bodhi"
summary = "**[]()Bodhi:** from verbal roo ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Bodhi:** from verbal root *budhi* to awaken, to understand: awakening, enlightenment, supreme knowledge. Through Bodhi one awakens from the slumber or stupor inflicted upon the mind by the defilements [*kilesa*](dic3_k.htm#kilesa) and comprehends the Four Noble Truths [*sacca*](dic3_s.htm#sacca) [Com.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Com.) to [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 10.

The enlightenment of a [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) is called [*sammā\-sambodhi*](dic3_s.htm#sammā-sambodhi) 'perfect enlightenment'. The faith [*saddhā*](dic3_s.htm#saddhā) of a lay follower of the [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) is described as he believes in the enlightenment of the Perfect One *saddahati Tathāgatassa bodhim:* [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 53, [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) III, 2.

As components of the state of enlightenment and contributory factors to its achievement, are mentioned in the texts: the 7 factors of enlightenment [*bojjhanga*](dic3_b.htm#bojjhanga) = [*bodhi\-anga*](dic3_b.htm#bodhi-anga) and the 37 'things pertaining to enlightenment' *bodhipakkhiya* \- *dhammā.* In one of the later books of the Sutta\-Pitaka, the Buddhavamsa, 10 [*bodhipācana\-dhammā*](dic3_b.htm#bodhipācana-dhammā) are mentioned, i.e. qualities that lead to the ripening of perfect enlightenment; these are the 10 perfections [*pāramī*](dic3_p.htm#pāramī).

There is a threefold classification of enlightenment: 1. that of a Noble Disciple [*sāvaka\-bodhi*](dic3_s.htm#sāvaka-bodhi). i.e. of an Arahat, 2. of an Independently Enlightened One [*pacceka\-bodhi*](dic3_p.htm#pacceka-bodhi), and 3. of a Perfect Enlightened One [*sammā\-sambodhi*](dic3_s.htm#sammā-sambodhi) This 3\-fold division, however, is of later origin, and in this form it neither occurs in the canonical texts nor in the older Sutta commentaries. The closest approximation to it is found in a verse sutta which is probably of a comparatively later period, the Treasure Store Sutta Nidhikkanda Sutta of the Khuddakapātha, where the following 3 terms are mentioned in stanza 15: *sāvaka\-pāramī, pacceka\-bodhi, buddha\-bhūmi* see [Khp.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Khp.) Tr., pp. 247f..

The commentaries e.g. to [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.), Buddhavamsa, Cariyapitaka generally give a 4\-fold explanation of the word bodhi: 1. the tree of enlightenment, 2. the Noble [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) [*ariya\-magga*](dic3_a.htm#ariya-magga), 3. Nibbāna, 4 omniscience of the Buddha: [*sabbaññutā* \-](dic3_s.htm#sabbaññutā-ñāna) [*ñāna*](dic3_n.htm#ñāna). As to 2, the commentaries quote Cula\-Nidesa where [*bodhi*](dic3_b.htm#bodhi) is defined as the knowledge relating to the 4 [paths](dic3_m.htm#magga) of Stream\-entry, etc.; [*catūsu,* *maggesu*](dic3_c.htm#catūsu%20maggesu%20ñāna).

Neither in the canonical texts nor in the old commentaries is it stated that a follower of the [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) may choose between the three kinds of enlightenment and aspire either to become a Buddha, a Pacceka\-Buddha, or an Arahat\-disciple. This conception of a choice between three aspirations is, however, frequently found in present\-day Theravāda countries, e.g. in Sri Lanka.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "bodhipakkhiya-dhammā"
summary = "**[]()Bodhipakkhiya\\-dhammā:** ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Bodhipakkhiya\-dhammā:** The 37 'things pertaining to enlightenment', or 'requisites of enlightenment' comprise the entire doctrines of the Buddha. They are:

>
>
>
>
> the 4 foundations of awareness or mindfulness [*satipatthāna*](dic3_s.htm#satipatthāna),  
> the 4 right efforts see: [*padhāna*](dic3_p.htm#padhāna),  
> the 4 roads to power [*iddhi\-pāda*](dic3_i.htm#iddhi-pāda),  
> the 5 spiritual abilities [*indriya*](dic3_i.htm#indriya), see: [*bala*](dic3_b.htm#bala),  
> the 5 spiritual powers [*bala*](dic3_b.htm#bala),  
> the 7 factors of enlightenment [*bojjhanga*](dic3_b.htm#bojjhanga),  
> the Noble 8\-fold [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) see: [*magga*](dic3_m.htm#magga).
>
>
>
>

In [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 77 all the 37 [*bodhipakkhiya\-dhammā*](dic3_b.htm#bodhipakkhiya-dhammā) are enumerated and explained though not called by that name. A detailed explanation of them is given in [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XXII. In [S.](dic2-abbrev.htm#S.) XLVII, 51, 67, only the five spiritual abilities [*indriya*](dic3_i.htm#indriya) are called *bodhipakkhiya* \- *dhammā* and in the Jhāna Vibhanga, only the 7 factors of enlightenment [*bojjhanga*](dic3_b.htm#bojjhanga).

>
>
>
>
> See The Requisites of Enlightenment, by Ledi Sayadaw [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [169/172](../Wheels/wh171.pdf).
>
>
>
>

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "bodhisatta"
summary = "**[]()Bodhisatta:** 'Enlighten ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Bodhisatta:** 'Enlightenment Being', is a being destined to Buddhahood, a future Buddha. According to the traditional belief a Bodhisatta, before reaching his last birth as a [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) on this earth, is living in the Tusita\-heaven see: [*deva*](dic3_d.htm#deva), the heaven of bliss. Cf. [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) IV, 127; VIII, 70.

In the Pāli Canon and commentaries, the designation 'Bodhisatta' is given only to Prince Siddhattha before his enlightenment and to his former existences. The [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) himself uses this term when speaking of his life prior to enlightenment e.g. [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 4, [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 26. Bodhisattahood is neither mentioned nor recommended as an ideal higher than or alternative to Arahatship; nor is there any record in the Pāli scriptures of a disciple declaring it as his aspiration. \- See [*bodhi*](dic3_b.htm#bodhi).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
```
``` toml
word = "bojjhanga"
summary = "**[]()Bojjhanga:** 'the 7 fact ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Bojjhanga:** 'the 7 factors of enlightenment', are: awareness or mindfulness [*sati\-sambojjhanga*](dic3_s.htm#sati-sambojjhanga), [*sati*](dic3_s.htm#sati), investigation of the law [*dhamma\-vicaya\-sambojjhanga*](dic3_d.htm#dhamma-vicaya-sambojjhanga) energy [*viriya\-sambojjhanga*](dic3_v.htm#viriya-sambojjhanga), [*viriya*](dic3_v.htm#viriya) [*padhāna*](dic3_p.htm#padhāna) rapture [*pīti*](dic3_p.htm#pīti) \- [*sambojjhanga*](dic3_s.htm#sambojjhanga) tranquillity [*passaddhi*](dic3_p.htm#passaddhi) \- [*sambojjhanga*](dic3_s.htm#sambojjhanga), concentration [*samādhi\-sambojjhanga*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi-sambojjhanga), equanimity *[upekkhā](dic3_u.htm#upekkhā).* Because they lead to enlightenment, therefore they are called factors of enlightenment see: XLVI, 5.

Though in the 2nd factor, [*dhamma*](dic3_d.htm#dhamma) \- *vicaya* the word [*dhamma*](dic3_d.htm#dhamma) is taken by most translators to stand for the Buddhist doctrine, it probably refers to the bodily and mental phenomena *nāma* \- [*rūpa*](dic3_r.htm#rūpa) \- *dhammā* as presented to the investigating mind by awareness or mindfulness, the 1st factor. With that interpretation, the term may be rendered by 'investigation of phenomena'.

In [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) X. 102, the 7 factors are said to be the means of attaining the threefold understanding see: *tevijjā.*

They may be attained by means of the 4 foundations of awareness or mindfulness [*satipatthāna*](dic3_s.htm#satipatthāna),, as it is said in see: XLVI, 1 and explained in [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 118:

>
>
>
>
> 1: Whenever, o Bhikkhus, the Bhikkhu dwells contemplating the body [*kāya*](dic3_k.htm#kāya) feeling [*vedanā*](dic3_v.htm#vedanā) mind [*citta*](dic3_c.htm#citta) and mental\-objects *dhammā* strenuous, clearly\-conscious, mindful, after subduing worldly greed and grief, at such a time his awareness or mindfulness is present and undisturbed; and whenever his awareness or mindfulness is present and undisturbed, at such a time he has gained and is developing the link to Awakening 'awareness or mindfulness' [*sati\-sambojjhanga*](dic3_s.htm#sati-sambojjhanga) and thus this link to Awakening reaches fullest perfection.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 2: Whenever, while dwelling with awareness or mindfulness, he wisely investigates, examines and thinks over the law… at such a time he has gained and is developing the link to Awakening 'investigation of the law' [*dhamma*](dic3_d.htm#dhamma) \- *vicaya* °…
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 3: Whenever, while wisely investigating his energy is firm and unshaken… at such a time he has gained and is developing the link to Awakening 'energy' [*viriya*](dic3_v.htm#viriya)…
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 4: Whenever in him, while firm in energy, arises supersense\-rapture… at such a time he has gained and is developing the link to Awakening 'rapture' *[pīti](dic3_p.htm#pīti)* °.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 5: Whenever, while enraptured in mind, his body and his mind become composed… at such a time he has gained and is developing the link to Awakening 'tranquillity' *[passaddhi](dic3_p.htm#passaddhi)* °
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 6: Whenever, while being composed in his body and happy, his mind becomes concentrated… at such a time he has gained and is developing the link to Awakening 'concentration' *[samādhi](dic3_s.htm#samādhi)* °
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 7: Whenever he looks with complete indifference on his mind thus concentrated… at such a time he has gained and is developing the link to Awakening 'equanimity' *[upekkhā](dic3_u.htm#upekkhā).*
>
>
>
>

>
>
>
>
> Literature: Bojjhanga Samyutta see: XLVI; Bojjhanga [Vibh.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vibh.) \- For the conditions leading to the arising of each of the factors, see the [Com.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Com.) to Satipatthāna Sutta Way of Mindfulness, by Soma Thera; 3rd ed., 1967, [BPS](dic2-abbrev.htm#BPS). Further, The 'Seven Factors of Enlightenment, by Piyadassi Thera [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [1.](../Wheels/wh001.pdf)
>
>
>
>

**[]()Brahma\-cariya:** 'pure chaste or Noble life', is a term for the life of the monk. Also a lay\-devotee who observes the 8 moral precepts [*sikkhāpada*](dic3_s.htm#sikkhāpada), takes as the third precept the vow of chastity, i.e. full abstention from sexual relations. The highest aim and purpose of **b.** is, according to [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 29, the 'unshakable deliverance of mind' *akuppā* *ceto* \- [*vimutti*](dic3_v.htm#vimutti).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "brahma-kāyika-deva"
summary = "**[]()Brahma\\-kāyika\\-deva:** ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Brahma\-kāyika\-deva:** The 'divine beings of the Brahma\-world' inhabit the first 3 heavens of the fine\-material world, *rūpaloka* corresponding to the 1st absorption [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna). The highest ruler of them is called the Great Brahma *mahā* \- *brahmā.* With caustic humor he is said [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 11 to pretend: I am Brahma, the Great Brahmā, the Most High, the Invincible One, the Omniscient One, the Ruler, the Lord, the Creator, the Maker, the Perfect One, the Preserver, the Controller, the Father of all that was and will be. Cf. [*deva*](dic3_d.htm#deva) II. 1\-3.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "brahma-loka"
summary = "**[]()Brahma\\-loka:** 'Brahma\\ ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Brahma\-loka:** 'Brahma\-world', in the widest sense, is a name for the fine\-material [*rūpa*](dic3_r.htm#rūpa) \- [*loka*](dic3_l.htm#loka) and immaterial world *arūpa* \- *loka;* in a narrower sense, however, only for the first three heavens of the fine\-material world. Cf. *brahma* \- *kāyika* \- [*deva*](dic3_d.htm#deva).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "brahma-vihāra"
summary = "**[]()Brahma\\-vihāra:** the 4 ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Brahma\-vihāra:** the 4 'sublime' or 'divine abodes', also called the 4 Infinite states [*appamaññā*](dic3_a.htm#appamaññā) are: loving\-kindness *[mettā](dic3_m.htm#mettā)* Pity [*karunā*](dic3_k.htm#karunā), altruistic or sympathetic joy *[muditā](dic3_m.htm#muditā)* equanimity *[upekkhā](dic3_u.htm#upekkhā).*

The stereotype text on the development of these 4 sublime abodes *brahma* \- *[vihāra](dic3_v.htm#vihāra)* \- *[bhāvanā](dic3_b.htm#bhāvanā)* *[bhāvanā](dic3_b.htm#bhāvanā)* often met with in the Suttas,\- is as follows: 'There, o Bhikkhus, the Bhikkhu with a mind full of loving\-kindness pervading first one direction, then a second one, then a third one, then the fourth one, just so above, below and all around; and everywhere identifying himself with all, he is pervading the whole world with mind full of loving\-kindness, with mind wide, developed, unbounded, free from hate and ill\-will. Hereafter follows the same theme with Pity, altruistic joy, and equanimity.

Literature: Detailed explanation in [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) IX. \- For texts see: [path](dic3_m.htm#magga), 97ff; texts on [*mettā*](dic3_m.htm#mettā) in The Practice of Loving Kindness, by ñānamoli Thera [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [7.](http://www.accesstoinsight.org/lib/authors/nanamoli/wheel007.html) \- The Four Sublime States, by Nyanaponika Thera [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [6.](http://www.accesstoinsight.org/lib/authors/nyanaponika/wheel006.html) \- Brahma Vihāra, by Narada Thera Vajirarama, Colombo, 1962.

``` toml
grammar = ""
```


**[]()Cakka:** 'wheel', is one of the seven 'precious possessions' *ratana* of a righteous World Emperor *cakkavatti* 'He who owns the Wheel,' cf. [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 26, and symbolizes conquering progress and expanding sovereignty. From that derives the figurative expression [*dhamma*](dic3_d.htm#dhamma) \- *cakkam* *pavatteti,* he sets rolling the Wheel of the Law' and the name of the Buddha’s first sermon, Dhamma\-cakkappavattana Sutta see: [*dhamma\-cakka*](dic3_d.htm#dhamma-cakka).

Another figurative meaning of C. is 'blessing'. There are 4 such 'auspicious wheels' or 'blessings': living in a suitable locality, company of good people, meritorious acts done in the past, right inclinations [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) IV, 31.

*[bhāva](dic3_b.htm#bhāva)* \- [*cakka*](dic3_c.htm#cakka) 'wheel of existence', or of life, is a name for 'dependent origination' see: *paticca\-samuppāda.*

>
>
>
>
> See The Buddhist Wheel Symbol, by T. B. Karunaratne [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [137/138](../Wheels/wh137.pdf); The Wheel of Birth and Death, by Bhikkhu Khantipalo [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [147/149](../Wheels/wh147.pdf)
>
>
>
>

[PTS](dic2-abbrev.htm#PTS), p. 235; the first 3 also in [It.](dic2-abbrev.htm#It.) 52: 1. the physical eye *mamsa* [*cakkhu*](dic3_c.htm#cakkhu). the divine eye [*dibba\-cakkhu*](dic3_d.htm#dibba-cakkhu) see: [*abhiññā*](dic3_a.htm#abhiññā),. the eye of understanding *[paññā](dic3_p.htm#paññā)* \- [*cakkhu*](dic3_c.htm#cakkhu) the eye of a [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) *buddha\- **c.**,* . the eye of all\-round knowledge *samanta* **c.;** a frequent appellation of the Buddha.

**[]()Catu\-vokāra\-bhava:** 'four\-group existence', is the existence in the immaterial world *arūpa* \- [*loka*](dic3_l.htm#loka) see: [*loka*](dic3_l.htm#loka) since only the four mental groups feeling, perception, mental constructions, consciousness, see: [*khandha*](dic3_k.htm#khandha) are found there, the materiality group being absent. Cf. *pañca\-vokāra\-bhava, eka\-vokāra\-bhava* [App.](dic2-abbrev.htm#App.): [*vokāra*](dic3_v.htm#vokāra).

**[]()Cetanā:** 'intention', will, is one of the seven mental properties [*cetasika*](dic3_c.htm#cetasika) inseparably bound up with all consciousness, namely sensorial or mental contact [*phassa*](dic3_p.htm#phassa) feeling [*vedanā*](dic3_v.htm#vedanā) perception *[saññā](dic3_s.htm#saññā)* intention *[cetanā](dic3_c.htm#cetanā),* concentration [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) vitality [*jīvita*](dic3_j.htm#jīvita) directing [*manasikāra*](dic3_m.htm#manasikāra) Cf. [Tab. II](table2.htm), III.

With regard to kammical intention i.e. advantageous or disadvantageous kamma it is said in [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) VI, 13:;intention is action kamma, thus I say, o Bhikkhus; for as soon as intention arises, one does the action, be it by body, speech or mind.; For details, see: [*paticca* \- *samuppāda*](dic3_p.htm#paticcasamuppāda) 10, kamma.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "cetasika"
summary = "**[]()Cetasika:** 'mental thin ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Cetasika:** 'mental things, mental properties', are those mental properties which are bound up with the simultaneously arising consciousness [*citta*](dic3_c.htm#citta) *=* [*viññāna*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna) and conditioned by its presence. Whereas in the Suttas all phenomena of existence are summed up under the aspect of 5 groups: materiality, feeling, perception, mental constructions, consciousness see: [*khandha*](dic3_k.htm#khandha) the Abhidhamma as a rule treats them under the more philosophical 3 aspects: consciousness, mental properties and materiality *citta, cetasika, rūpa* Thus, of these 3 aspects, the mental properties [*cetasika*](dic3_c.htm#cetasika) comprise feeling, perception and the 50 mental constructions, altogether 52 mental properties. Of these, 25 are lofty qualities either kammically advantageous or neutral, 14 kammically disadvantageous, while 13 are as such kammically neutral, their kammical quality depending on whether they are associated with advantageous, disadvantageous or neutral consciousness. For details see: [Tab. II](table2.htm), III. Cf. prec. App.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "cetaso vinibandha"
summary = "**[[cetaso vinibandha]]Cetaso ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[[cetaso vinibandha]]Cetaso vinibandha:** 'mental bondages', are 5 things which hinder the mind from making right exertion, namely: lust for sense\-objects, for the body, for visible things, for eating and sleeping, and leading the monk’s life for the sake of divine rebirth. For details, see: [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) V, 205; X, 14; [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 33; [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 16. Cf. foll.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "ceto-pariya-ñāna"
summary = "**[]()Ceto\\-pariya\\-ñāna:** 'p ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Ceto\-pariya\-ñāna:** 'penetrating knowledge of the mind of others', is one of the 6 higher powers [*abhiññā*](dic3_a.htm#abhiññā) 3.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "ceto-vimutti"
summary = "**[]()Ceto\\-vimutti:** 'delive ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Ceto\-vimutti:** 'deliverance of mind'. In the highest sense it signifies the fruition of Arahatship see: [*ariya\-puggala*](dic3_a.htm#ariya-puggala) and in particular, the concentration associated with it. It is often linked with the 'deliverance through understanding' [*paññā\-vimutti*](dic3_p.htm#paññā-vimutti),, e.g. in the ten powers of a Perfect One see: *dasa* \- [*bala*](dic3_b.htm#bala) See [*vimokkha*](dic3_v.htm#vimokkha) I.

It is also called 'unshakable deliverance of mind' *akuppa* further 'Infinite of m'. *appamāna* d. of m. from the conditions of existence, or signless of m.' *animittā* d. of m. from the appendages' *ākincañña* **c.** since that state of mind is free from the 3 bonds, conditions and appendants, i.e. from greed, hatred and ignorance; and since it is void thereof, it is called the 'void deliverance of mind' *suññatā\- \*c.\**

In a more restricted sense, 'Infinite deliverance of mind' is a name for the 4 Infinite states, i.e. loving\-kindness, Pity, altruistic joy and equanimity see: *brahma\-vihāra; d. of m. from the appendages stands for the sphere of nothingness ākiñcaññāyatana* see: [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna) 7; 'd. of mind from the conditions of existence', for of mind due to non\-attention to all conditions of existence; 'void of m' for of m. due to contemplating voidness of self. For further details, see: [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 43.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "cetokhila"
summary = "**[]()Cetokhila:** 'mental obd ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Cetokhila:** 'mental obduracies', are 5 things which stiffen and hinder the mind from making right exertion, namely: doubt about the Master, about the Doctrine, about the Noble Brotherhood, about the training, and anger against one’s fellow\-Bhikkhus. For details [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) V, 206, X 14; [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 33; [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 16. Cf. prec.

``` toml
inflections = []
```

**[]()Chal\-abhiñño:** an Arahat who is a 'possessor of the 6 higher powers' see: [*abhiññā*](dic3_a.htm#abhiññā).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
```
``` toml
word = "chanda"
summary = "**[]()Chanda:** intention, des ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Chanda:** intention, desire, will.

>
>
>
>
> 1. As an ethically neutral psychological term, in the sense of 'intention', it is one of those general mental properties [*cetasika*](dic3_c.htm#cetasika) [Tab. II](table2.htm) taught in the Abhidhamma, the moral quality of which is determined by the character of the intention *[cetanā](dic3_c.htm#cetanā)* associated therewith. The [Com.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Com.) explains it as 'a wish to do' *kattu* \- *kamyatā* \- [*chanda*](dic3_c.htm#chanda) If intensified, it acts also as a 'predominance condition' see: [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) 3.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 2. As an evil quality it has the meaning of 'desire', and is frequently coupled with terms for 'sensuality', 'greed', etc., for instance: [*kāma\-cchanda*](dic3_k.htm#kāma-cchanda), sense\-desire', one of the 5 hindrances see: [*nīvarana*](dic3_n.htm#nīvarana) [*chanda*](dic3_c.htm#chanda) \- [*rāga*](dic3_r.htm#rāga) 'lustful desire' see: [*kāma*](dic3_k.htm#kāma) It is one of the 4 wrong [paths](dic3_m.htm#magga) see: [*agati*](dic3_a.htm#agati).
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 3. As a good quality it is a righteous will or alertness [*dhamma*](dic3_d.htm#dhamma) \- [*chanda*](dic3_c.htm#chanda) and occurs, e.g. in the formula of the 4 right efforts see: [*padhāna*](dic3_p.htm#padhāna) The Bhikkhu rouses his will *chandam* *janeti.* ..; If intensified, it is one of the 4 roads to power see: *iddhipāda*
>
>
>
>

**[]()Citta:** 'mind', 'consciousness', 'state of consciousness', is a synonym of [*mano*](dic3_m.htm#mano) and [*viññāna*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna) see: [*khandha*](dic3_k.htm#khandha) and [Tab.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Tab.) 1. [Dhs](dic2-abbrev.htm#Dhs.) divides all phenomena into consciousness [*citta*](dic3_c.htm#citta) mental properties [*cetasika*](dic3_c.htm#cetasika) and materiality [*rūpa*](dic3_r.htm#rūpa).

In *adhicitta* 'higher mentality', it signifies the concentrated, quietened mind, and is one of the 3 trainings see: *[sikkhā](dic3_s.htm#sikkhā)* The concentration or intensification of consciousness is one of the 4 roads to power see: *iddhipāda.*

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"

inflections = []
```

**[[citta\-ja (citta\-samutthāna)\-rūpa]]Citta\-ja citta\-samutthāna\-rūpa:** 'mind\-produced materiality'; see: [*samutthāna*](dic3_s.htm#samutthāna)


**[]()Citta\-kammaññatā:** *°lahutā, °mudutā, °paguññatā, °passaddhi, °ujukatā* see: [Tab. II.](table2.htm)

``` toml
summary = "**[]()Citta\\-kkhana:** 'consci ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Citta\-kkhana:** 'consciousness\-moment', is the time occupied by one single stage in the perceptual process or cognitive series *cittavīthi* see: [*viññāna\-kicca*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna-kicca) This moment again is subdivided into the genetic *uppāda* static *thiti* and dissolving *bhanga* moment. One such moment is said in the commentaries to be of inconceivably short duration and to last not longer than the billionth part of the time occupied by a flash of lightning. However that may be, we ourselves know from experience that it is possible within one single second to dream of innumerable things and events. In [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) I, 10 it is said:;Nothing, o Bhikkhus, do I know that changes so rapidly as consciousness. Scarcely anything may be found that could be compared with this so rapidly changing consciousness.; [App.](dic2-abbrev.htm#App.) [*khana*](dic3_k.htm#khana).

**[]()Gotrabhū:** lit. 'who has entered the lineage of the Noble Ones', i.e. the Matured One.

I. 'change\-of\-lineage\-Moment' *gotrabhū* \- [*citta*](dic3_c.htm#citta) is the last of the 4 impulse moments [*javana*](dic3_j.htm#javana) cf. [*viññāna\-kicca*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna-kicca) immediately preceding the entering into an absorption [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna) or into one of the supra\-mundane [paths](dic3_m.htm#magga) see: [*ariya\-puggala*](dic3_a.htm#ariya-puggala) [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.). Cf. [*visuddhi*](dic3_v.htm#visuddhi) VII.

II. The 'Matured One'.;He who is endowed with those things, immediately upon which follows the entrance into the noble [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) [*ariya\-magga*](dic3_a.htm#ariya-magga), this person is called a 'Matured One'.; Pug 10. In the [Com.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Com.) to this passage it is said:;He who through perceiving Nibbāna, leaves behind the whole multitude of worldlings [*puthujjana*](dic3_p.htm#puthujjana), the family of worldlings, the circle of worldlings, the designation of a worldling and enters into the multitude of the Noble Ones, the family of the Noble Ones, the circle of the Noble Ones, and obtains the designation of a Noble One, such a being is called a Matured One.; By this state of consciousness is meant the lightning\-like transitional stage between the state of a worldling and that of a *[sotāpanna](dic3_s.htm#sotāpanna)* see: [*ariya\-puggala*](dic3_a.htm#ariya-puggala) \- Gotrabhū is mentioned in this sense, i.e. as 9th *[ariya\-puggala](dic3_a.htm#ariya-puggala),* in [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) IX, 10; X, 16.

**[]()Hadaya\-vatthu:** 'heart as physical base' of mental life. The heart, according to the commentaries as well as to the general Buddhist tradition, forms the physical base [*vatthu*](dic3_v.htm#vatthu) of consciousness In the canonical texts, however, even in the Abhidhamma Pitaka, no such base is ever localized, a fact which seems to have first been discovered by Shwe Zan Aung Compendium of Philosophy, pp. 277ff.. In the [Patth.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Patth.) we find repeatedly only the passage:;That material thing based on which mind\-element and mind\-consciousness element function; *yam rūpam nissāya manodhātu ca mano\-viññāna\-dhātu ca vattanti, tam rūpam.*

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
```
``` toml
word = "hetu"
summary = "**[]()Hetu:** 'cause', conditi ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Hetu:** 'cause', condition, reason; Abhidhamma root\-condition. In sutta usage it is almost synonymous with [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) 'condition', and often occurs together with it 'What is the cause, what is the condition', *ko* [*hetu*](dic3_h.htm#hetu) *ko* *paccayo.*

In Abhidhamma, it denotes the advantageous and disadvantageous roots [*mūla*](dic3_m.htm#mūla). In that sense, as 'root\-condition' [*hetu*](dic3_h.htm#hetu) \- [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) see. [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) it is the first of the 24 conditions given in the introduction to the Patthāna see: [Guide](dic2-abbrev.htm#Guide), p. 117. The Dhs 1052\-1082 and Patthāna Duka\-patth; [Guide](dic2-abbrev.htm#Guide), p. 144 have sections on roots hetu. \- The term is also used a for the classification of consciousness, as *sa* \- *hetuka* and *a* \- *hetuka* with and without concomitant root\-conditions; b for a division of rebirth consciousness into *ahetuka* *dvihetuka* and *tihetuka* without, with 2, or with 3 root\-conditions see: [*patisandhi*](dic3_p.htm#patisandhi)

*ahetuka* \- [*ditthi*](dic3_d.htm#ditthi) the false view of the uncausedness of existence; see: [*ditthi*](dic3_d.htm#ditthi)

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
```

``` toml
summary = "**[]()Hiri\\-ottappa:** 'moral ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Hiri\-ottappa:** 'moral shame and Fear of Wrongdoing', are associated with all kammically advantageous consciousness see: [Tab. II.](table2.htm)

To be ashamed of what one ought to be ashamed of, to be ashamed of performing evil and disadvantageous things: this is called moral shame. To be in dread of what one ought to be in dread of, to be in dread of performing evil and disadvantageous things: this is called Fear of Wrongdoing; Pug, 79, 80.

Two lucid things, o Bhikkhus, protect the world: moral shame and Fear of Wrongdoing. If these two things were not to protect the world, then one would respect neither one’s mother, nor one’s mother’s sister, nor one’s brother’s wife, nor one’s teacher’s wife.; [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) II, 7. Cf. *ahirika* See [Atthasālini](dic2-abbrev.htm#Atthasālini) Tr. I. pp. 164ff.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
```
``` toml
word = "hāna-bhāgiya-sīla"
summary = "**[]()Hāna\\-bhāgiya\\-sīla: \\-* ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Hāna\-bhāgiya\-sīla: \-** [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) b h. b. p *[aññā](dic3_p.htm#paññā)* morality, concentration or understanding connected with decline. The other three stages are: [*thiti\-bhāgiya\-sīla*](dic3_t.htm#thiti-bhāgiya-sīla) etc. morality, etc. connected with a standstill; *visesa* \- *bhāgiya* [*sīla*](dic3_s.htm#sīla) etc.: morality, etc. connected with progress; *nibbedha* \- *bhāgiya* [*sīla*](dic3_s.htm#sīla) etc.: morality, etc. connected with penetration. Cf. [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) IV, 179; VI. X, 71.

'Decline' *hāna* is to be understood with regard to the arising of opposing qualities, 'standstill' *thiti* with regard to the standstill of the corresponding attentiveness, 'progress' *visesa* with regard to higher excellency, 'penetration' *nibbedha* with regard to the arising of perception and reflection connected with the turning away from existence; [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) III. Cf. [*vodāna*](dic3_v.htm#vodāna) 2.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "iddhi"
summary = "**[]()Iddhi:** 'power', 'magic ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Iddhi:** 'power', 'magical power'. The magical powers constitute one of the 6 kinds of higher spiritual powers [*abhiññā*](dic3_a.htm#abhiññā). One distinguishes many kinds of magical powers: the power of determination *adhitthān* [*iddhi*](dic3_i.htm#iddhi) i.e. the power of becoming oneself many; the power of transconstruction *vikubbana* [*iddhi*](dic3_i.htm#iddhi) i.e. the power of adopting another form; the power of spiritual creation *manomaya* [*iddhi*](dic3_i.htm#iddhi) i.e. the power of letting issue from this body another mentally produced body; the power of penetrating knowledge [*ñāna*](dic3_n.htm#ñāna) \- *vipphara* [*iddhi*](dic3_i.htm#iddhi) i.e. the power of inherent insight to remain unhurt in danger; the power of penetrating concentration *samādhivippharā* [*iddhi*](dic3_i.htm#iddhi) producing the same result. The magical powers are treated in detail in [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XII; [Pts.M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Pts.M.), [Vibh.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vibh.) \- [App.](dic2-abbrev.htm#App.). They are not a necessary condition for final deliverance.

'Noble power' *ariyā* \- [*iddhi*](dic3_i.htm#iddhi) is the power of controlling one’s ideas in such a way that one may consider something not repulsive as repulsive and something repulsive as not repulsive, and remain all the time imperturbable and full of equanimity. This training of mind is frequently mentioned in the Suttas e.g. [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 152, [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) V. 144, but only once the name of *ariyā* \- [*iddhi*](dic3_i.htm#iddhi) is applied to it [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 28. See further [Pts.M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Pts.M.), Iddhi\-kathā, [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XII.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "iddhi-pāda"
summary = "**[]()Iddhi\\-pāda:** 'roads to ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Iddhi\-pāda:** 'roads to power' or success are the 4 following qualities,,for as guides, they indicate the road to power connected therewith; and because they form, by way of preparation, the roads to the power constituting the fruition of the [path](dic3_m.htm#magga); [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XII, namely:;concentration of intention [*chanda*](dic3_c.htm#chanda) \- [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) accompanied by effort of will [*padhāna*](dic3_p.htm#padhāna) \- [*sankhāra*](dic3_s.htm#sankhāra) \- *samannāgata* concentration of energy *[viriya](dic3_v.htm#viriya)* \- [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi)… concentration of consciousness [*citta*](dic3_c.htm#citta) \- [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi).. and concentration of investigation *vimamsa* \- [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) accompanied by effort of will.; As such, they are supra\-mundane [*lokuttara*](dic3_l.htm#lokuttara) i.e. connected with the [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) or the fruition of the [path](dic3_m.htm#magga); see: *[ariya\-puggala](dic3_a.htm#ariya-puggala)* But they are mundane [*lokiya*](dic3_l.htm#lokiya) as predominant factors [*adhipati*](dic3_a.htm#adhipati) see: [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya), for it is said:;Because the monk, through making intention a predominant factor, reaches concentration, it is called the concentration of intention [*chanda*](dic3_c.htm#chanda) \- [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) etc.; [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XII.

These 4 roads of power lead to the attaining and acquiring of magical power, to the power of magical transconstruction, to the generation of magical power, and to mastery and skill therein; [Pts.M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Pts.M.) II. 205, [PTS](dic2-abbrev.htm#PTS). For a detailed explanation, see: [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XII.

Once the Bhikkhu has thus developed and often practised the 4 roads to power, he enjoys various magical powers,… hears with the divine ear divine and human sounds,… perceives with his mind the mind of other beings… remembers many a former existence… perceives with the divine eye beings passing away and reappearing,… attains, after the ceasing of fermentations, deliverance of mind and deliverance through understanding, free from. fermentations. see: LI, 2. For a detailed explanation of these 6 higher powers, see: [*abhiññā*](dic3_a.htm#abhiññā)

Whosoever, o Bhikkhus, has missed the 4 roads to power, he has missed the right [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) leading to the ceasing of suffering; but whosoever, o Bhikkhus, has reached the 4 roads to power, he has reached the right [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) leading to the ceasing of suffering; see: LI, 2.

>
>
>
>
> See the chapter on Iddhipāda in The Requisites of Enlightenment by Ledi Sayadaw [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [169/172](../Wheels/wh171.pdf).
>
>
>
>

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
```
``` toml
word = "indriya"
summary = "**[]()Indriya:** 'abilities', ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Indriya:** 'abilities', is a name for 22, partly physical, partly mental, phenomena often treated in the Suttas as well as in the Abhidhamma. They are:

>
>
>
>
> 6 Bases [*āyatana*](dic3_a.htm#āyatana):
>
>
>
>

1. eye: [*cakkhu*](dic3_c.htm#cakkhu)  
2. ear: *sota*  
3. nose: *ghāna*  
4. tongue: *jivhā*  
5. body: [*kāya*](dic3_k.htm#kāya)  
6. mind: *mano*

>
>
>
>
> Gender [*bhava*](dic3_b.htm#bhava):
>
>
>
>

7. femininity: *itthi*  
8. masculinity: *purisa*  
9. vitality: *jīvita*

>
>
>
>
> 5 Feelings [*vedanā*](dic3_v.htm#vedanā) q. v.
>
>
>
>

10. bodily pleasant feeling: [*sukha*](dic3_s.htm#sukha)  
11. bodily pain: [*dukkha*](dic3_d.htm#dukkha)  
12. gladness: [*somanassa*](dic3_s.htm#somanassa)  
13. sadness: [*domanassa*](dic3_d.htm#domanassa)  
14. indifference: *[upekkhā](dic3_u.htm#upekkhā)*

>
>
>
>
> 5 Spiritual Abilities see: *bala*
>
>
>
>

15. []()faith: *[saddhā](dic3_s.htm#saddhā)*  
16. energy: [*viriya*](dic3_v.htm#viriya)  
17. awareness or mindfulness: [*sati*](dic3_s.htm#sati)  
18. concentration: [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi)  
19. understanding: *[]()paññā*

>
>
>
>
> 3 supra\-mundane Abilities
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 20. the assurance: 'I shall know what I did not yet know!': *aññātañ\-ñassāmīt' indriya*  
> 21. the ability of highest knowledge: [*aññindriya*](dic3_a.htm#aññindriya)  
> 22. the ability of him who knows: [*aññātāvindriya*](dic3_a.htm#aññātāvindriya)
>
>
>
>

1\-5, 7\-8 are physical; 9 is either physical or mental. All the rest are mental. \- 14 see: *[upekkhā](dic3_u.htm#upekkhā)* is here merely indifferent feeling = *adukkha* \- *m* \- *asukhā* *[vedanā](dic3_v.htm#vedanā)* i.e. 'neither pleasant nor unpleasant feeling' and not identical with that highly ethical state of equanimity = *tatramajjhattatā* i.e. 'keeping everywhere the middle', the equipoise of mind, also called *[upekkhā](dic3_u.htm#upekkhā)* which belongs to the group of mental constructions [*sankhāra*](dic3_s.htm#sankhāra) \- *[khandha](dic3_k.htm#khandha)* see: Tab II. \- 20 arises at the moment of entering the Sotāpatti\- [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) [*sotāpatti*](dic3_s.htm#sotāpatti) \- [*magga*](dic3_m.htm#magga) 21 on reaching the Sotāpatti\-Fruition [*sotāpatti*](dic3_s.htm#sotāpatti) \- [*phala*](dic3_p.htm#phala) 22 at attaining the Arahat\-Fruition *arahatta* \- [*phala*](dic3_p.htm#phala) For the three last, see: [*ariya\-puggala*](dic3_a.htm#ariya-puggala)

The abilities, excepting 7 and 8, form one of the 24 conditions [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) 6.

In [Vibh.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vibh.) V all these abilities are treated in the above order, whereas see: XLVIII enumerates and explains them by way of the above indicated groups, leaving only 20\-22 unexplained. See Vis XVI; [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) 138ff. \- For the 5 spiritual abilities 15\-19, see: The Way of Wisdom [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [65/66.](../Wheels/wh065.pdf)

``` toml
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Indriya\-paccaya:** see: [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) 16.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "indriya-samatta"
summary = "**[]()Indriya\\-samatta:** 'equ ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Indriya\-samatta:** 'equilibrium, balance, or harmony of abilities', relates to the 5 spiritual abilities: faith, energy, awareness or mindfulness, concentration and understanding see: [*indriya*](dic3_i.htm#indriya) 15\-19. Of these there are two pairs of abilities, in each of which both abilities should well counter\-balance each other, namely: faith and understanding *[saddhā](dic3_s.htm#saddhā)* *[paññā](dic3_p.htm#paññā)* on the one hand and energy and concentration [*viriya*](dic3_v.htm#viriya) [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) on the other. For excessive faith with deficient understanding leads to blind belief, whilst excessive understanding with deficient faith leads to cunning. In the same way, great energy with weak concentration leads to restlessness, whilst strong concentration with deficient energy leads to indolence. Though for both abilities in each of the 2 pairs a balanced degree of intensity is desirable, awareness or mindfulness should be allowed to develop to the highest degree of strength. Cf. [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) III\- [App.](dic2-abbrev.htm#App.).

**[]()Investigation:** full understanding through: *tīranapariññā* see: *[pariññā](dic3_p.htm#pariññā)* \- 'Investigation' *vīmamsā* is one of the 4 roads to power *iddhipāda* and one of the 4 predominants [*adhipati*](dic3_a.htm#adhipati) s [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) 3. \- **i.** of truth: [*dhamma*](dic3_d.htm#dhamma) \- *vicaya* is one of the 7 factors of enlightenment [*bojjhanga*](dic3_b.htm#bojjhanga).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "iriyā-patha"
summary = "**[]()Iriyā\\-patha:** lit. 'wa ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Iriyā\-patha:** lit. 'ways of movement': 'bodily postures', i.e. going, standing, sitting, lying. In the Satipatthāna\-sutta see: [*satipatthāna*](dic3_s.htm#satipatthāna) they form the subject of a contemplation and an exercise in awareness or mindfulness.

While going, standing, sitting or lying down, the Bhikkhu knows 'I go', 'I stand', 'I sit', 'I lie down'; he understands any position of the body.; \-;The disciple understands that there is no living being, no real ego, that goes, stands, etc., but that it is by a mere figure of speech that one says: 'I go', 'I stand', and so forth.; [Com.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Com.).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "issā"
summary = "**[]()\\*Issā:**\\* 'envy', is a ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()\*Issā:**\* 'envy', is a kammically disadvantageous [*akusala*](dic3_a.htm#akusala) mental property, which is occasionally associated with hate\-rooted consciousness see: [Tab. I](table1.htm). 30, 31. Explained in [Pug.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Pug.) 55.

**[]()Jarā:** 'old age, decay', is one of the 3 divine messengers see: [*deva\-dūta*](dic3_d.htm#deva-dūta). For its conditioning by birth, see: [*paticcasamuppāda*](dic3_p.htm#paticcasamuppāda) 11.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "javana"
summary = "**[]()Javana:** fr. *javati* t ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Javana:** fr. *javati* to impel: 'impulsion', is the phase of full cognition in the cognitive series, or perceptual process [*citta\-vīthi*](dic3_c.htm#citta-vīthi) see. [*viññāna\-kicca*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna-kicca) occurring at its climax, if the respective object is large or distinct. It is at this phase that kamma is produced, i.e. advantageous or disadvantageous intention concerning the perception that was the object of the previous stages of the respective process of consciousness. There are normally 7 impulse moments. In mundane consciousness [*lokiya*](dic3_l.htm#lokiya), any of the 17 kammically advantageous classes of consciousness [Tab. I](table1.htm), 1\-17 or of the 12 disadvantageous ones [Tab. I](table1.htm), 22\-23 may arise at the phase of impulsion. For the Arahat, however, impulsion has no longer a kammic, i.e. rebirth\-producing character, but is a kammically independent function [*kiriya*](dic3_k.htm#kiriya) [Tab. I](table1.htm), 72\-89. There are further 8 supra\-mundane classes of impulsion [Tab. I](table1.htm), 18\-21, 66\-69.

The 4 impulse moments immediately before entering an absorption [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna) or one of the supra\-mundane [paths](dic3_m.htm#magga) [*magga*](dic3_m.htm#magga) see. *[ariya\-puggala](dic3_a.htm#ariya-puggala)* are: the preparatory [*parikamma*](dic3_p.htm#parikamma) approach [*upacāra*](dic3_u.htm#upacāra) adaptation *anuloma* and change\-of\-lineage\-moment *[gotrabhū](dic3_g.htm#gotrabhū)* In connection with entering the earth\-kasina absorption see: [*kasina*](dic3_k.htm#kasina) they are explained as follows, in [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) IV:;After the breaking off of the subconscious stream of being [*bhavanga\-sota*](dic3_b.htm#bhavanga-sota), there arises the 'directing at the mind\-door' *manodvārāvajjana* see: *viññānakicca,* taking as object the earthkasina whilst thinking, 'Earth! Earth!' Thereupon, 4 or 5 impulse moments flash forth, amongst which the last one change\-of\-lineage\-moment belongs to the fine\-material sphere [*rūpāvacara*](dic3_r.htm#rūpāvacara) whereas the rest belong to the sense\-sphere [*kāmāvacara*](dic3_k.htm#kāmāvacara), see: [*avacara*](dic3_a.htm#avacara) though the last one is more powerful in thought conception, discursive thinking, interest rapture, joy and concentration cf. [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna) than the states of consciousness belonging to the sense\-sphere. They are called 'preparatory' [*parikamma\-samādhi*](dic3_p.htm#parikamma-samādhi) as they are preparing for the attainment\-concentration *appanā* \- *samādhi;* access [*upacāra\-samādhi*](dic3_u.htm#upacāra-samādhi) as they are close to the attainment\-concentration and are moving in its neighbourhood; adaptive *anuloma* as they adapt themselves to the preceding preparatory states and to the succeeding attainment concentration. The last one of the four is called 'matured' gotrabhū. In a similar way, the impulse moments before reaching the divine ear are described in [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XIII, 1. \- Cf. Kamma \- [App.](dic2-abbrev.htm#App.).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "jewels"
summary = "**[]()Jewels:** The 3: [*ti\\-r ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Jewels:** The 3: [*ti\-ratana*](dic3_t.htm#ti-ratana)

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "jhāna"
summary = "**[]()Jhāna:** 'absorption' me ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Jhāna:** 'absorption' meditation refers chiefly to the four meditative absorptions of the fine\-material sphere [*rūpa\-jjhāna*](dic3_r.htm#rūpa-jjhāna) or [*rūpāvacara*](dic3_r.htm#rūpāvacara) \- *jjhāna* [*avacara*](dic3_a.htm#avacara) They are achieved through the attainment of full or attainment \-, or ecstatic concentration *appanā* see: [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) during which there is a complete, though temporary, suspension of fivefold sense\-activity and of the 5 hindrances see: [*nīvarana*](dic3_n.htm#nīvarana) The state of consciousness, however, is one of full alertness and lucidity. This high degree of concentration is generally developed by the practice of one of the 40 subjects of tranquillity meditation [*samatha*](dic3_s.htm#samatha) \- [*kammatthāna*](dic3_k.htm#kammatthāna) see. *[bhāvanā](dic3_b.htm#bhāvanā)* Often also the 4 immaterial spheres *arūpāyatana* are called absorptions of the immaterial sphere [*arūpa\-jjhāna*](dic3_a.htm#arūpa-jjhāna) or *[arūpāvacara](dic3_a.htm#arūpāvacara)* \- *jjhāna* The stereotype text, often met with in the Suttas, runs as follows:

>
>
>
>
> 1;Detached from sensual objects, o Bhikkhus, detached from disadvantageous consciousness, attached with thought\-conception vitakka and discursive thinking [*vicāra*](dic3_v.htm#vicāra), born of detachment *vivekaja* and filled with rapture [*pīti*](dic3_p.htm#pīti) and joy [*sukha*](dic3_s.htm#sukha) he enters the first absorption.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 2;After the subsiding of thought\-conception and discursive thinking, and by gaining inner tranquillity and oneness of mind, he enters into a state free from thought\-conception and discursive thinking, the second absorption, which is born of concentration [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) and filled with rapture [*pīti*](dic3_p.htm#pīti) and joy [*sukha*](dic3_s.htm#sukha).
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 3;After the fading away of rapture he dwells in equanimity, mindful, clearly conscious; and he experiences in his person that feeling of which the Noble Ones say, 'Happy lives the man of equanimity and attentive mind'; thus he enters the 3rd absorption.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 4;After having given up pleasure and pain, and through the disappearance of previous joy and grief, he enters into a state beyond pleasure and pain, into the 4th absorption, which is purified by equanimity *[upekkhā](dic3_u.htm#upekkhā)* and awareness or mindfulness.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 5;Through the total overcoming of the perceptions of matter, however, and through the vanishing of sense\-reactions and the non\-attention to the perceptions of variety, with the idea, 'Infinite is space', he reaches the sphere of Infinite space [*ākāsānañcāyatana*](dic3_a.htm#ākāsānañcāyatana) and abides therein.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> (By 'perceptions of matter' [*rūpa*](dic3_r.htm#rūpa) \- *[saññā](dic3_s.htm#saññā)* are meant the absorptions of the fine\-material sphere, as well as those objects themselves… [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) X, 1.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> By 'perceptions of sense\-reactions' [*patigha*](dic3_p.htm#patigha) \- *[saññā](dic3_s.htm#saññā)* are meant those perceptions that have arisen due to the impact of sense\-organs eye, etc. and the sense\-objects visible objects, etc.. They are a name for the perception of visible objects, as it is said Jhāna\-Vibh.: 'What are here the perceptions of sense\-reactions? They are the perceptions of visible objects, sounds, etc.' \- Surely, they do no longer exist even for one who has entered the 1st absorption, etc., for at such a time the five\-sense consciousness is no longer functioning. Nevertheless, this is to be understood as having been said in praise of this immaterial absorption, in order to incite the striving for it; [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) X, 16.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> Perceptions of variety *ñānatta* \- *[saññā](dic3_s.htm#saññā)* are the perceptions that arise in various fields, or the various perceptions; ib.. Hereby, according to [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) X, 20, are meant the multiform perceptions outside the absorptions.)
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 6;Through the total overcoming of the sphere of Infinite space, and with the idea 'Infinite is consciousness', he reaches the sphere of Infinite consciousness *[viññānañcāyatana](dic3_v.htm#viññānañcāyatana)* and abides therein.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 7;Through the total overcoming of the sphere of Infinite consciousness, and with the idea 'Nothing is there', he reaches the sphere of nothingness [*ākiñcaññāyatana*](dic3_a.htm#ākiñcaññāyatana) and abides therein.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 8;Through the total overcoming of the sphere of nothingness he reaches the sphere of neither\-perception\-nor\-non\-perception *nevasaññā* \- *n’asaññāyatana* and abides therein
>
>
>
>

Thus the 1st absorption is free from 5 things i.e. the hindrances, [*nīvarana*](dic3_n.htm#nīvarana), and 5 things are present i.e. the factors of absorption; [*jhānanga*](dic3_j.htm#jhānanga) Whenever the Bhikkhu enters the 1st absorption, there have vanished sense\-desire, ill\-will, lethargy and Laziness, restlessness and regrets, doubts; and there are present: thought\-conception *vitakka* discursive thinking [*vicāra*](dic3_v.htm#vicāra) rapture [*pīti*](dic3_p.htm#pīti), joy [*sukha*](dic3_s.htm#sukha) and concentration [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) In the 2nd absorption there are present: rapture, joy and concentration; in the 3rd: joy and concentration; in the 4th: equanimity *[upekkhā](dic3_u.htm#upekkhā)* and concentration; [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) IV.

The 4 absorptions of the immaterial sphere see: above 5\-8 still belong, properly speaking, to the 4th absorption as they possess the same two constituents. The 4th fine\-material absorption is also the base or starting point *pādaka* \- [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna) for the attaining of the higher spiritual powers [*abhiññā*](dic3_a.htm#abhiññā).

In the Abhidhamma, generally a fivefold instead of a fourfold division of the fine\-material absorptions is used: the 2nd absorption has still the constituent 'discursive thinking' but without thought\-conception, while the 3rd, 4th and 5th correspond to the 2nd, 3rd and 4th, respectively, of the fourfold division see: [Tab. I](table1.htm), 9\- 13. This fivefold division is based on sutta texts like A. VIII, 63.

For the 8 absorptions as objects for the development of insight *[vipassanā](dic3_v.htm#vipassanā),* see samatha\- *[vipassanā](dic3_v.htm#vipassanā)* \- Full details in [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) IV\-X.

Jhāna in its widest sense e.g. as one of the 24 conditions; see: [paccaya](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) 17, denotes any, even momentary or weak absorption of mind, when directed on a single object.

``` toml
summary = "**[]()Jhāna\\-paccaya:** is one ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Jhāna\-paccaya:** is one of the 24 conditions [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya).

``` toml
inflections = []
```

**[]()Joy:** [*somanassa*](dic3_s.htm#somanassa) \- Altruistic **j.** = *[muditā](dic3_m.htm#muditā)* see: [*brahma\-vihāra*](dic3_b.htm#brahma-vihāra).

**[]()Jāti:** 'birth', comprises the entire embryonic process beginning with conception and ending with parturition.

The birth of beings belonging to this or that order of beings, their being born, their conception [*okkanti*](dic3_o.htm#okkanti) and springing into existence, the manifestation of the groups materiality, feeling, perception, mental constructions, consciousness; see: [*khandha*](dic3_k.htm#khandha) the acquiring of their sensitive organs: this is called birth; [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 22. For its conditioning by the prenatal kamma\-making [*kamma\-bhava*](dic3_k.htm#kamma-bhava) see. [*bhava*](dic3_b.htm#bhava) [*paticcasamuppāda*](dic3_p.htm#paticcasamuppāda) 9, 10, [*patisandhi*](dic3_p.htm#patisandhi)

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "jīva"
summary = "**[]()Jīva:** life, vital prin ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Jīva:** life, vital principle, individual soul. 'Soul life and body are identical' and 'Soul and body are different', these two frequently quoted wrong views fall under the 2 kinds of personality\-belief [*sakkāya\-ditthi*](dic3_s.htm#sakkāya-ditthi) see: [*ditthi*](dic3_d.htm#ditthi) i.e. the first one under the annihilation\-belief [*uccheda\-ditthi*](dic3_u.htm#uccheda-ditthi) and the second under the eternity\-belief [*sassata\-ditthi*](dic3_s.htm#sassata-ditthi).

Verily, if one holds the view that the soul life is identical with the body, in that case a Noble life is not possible; or if one holds the view that the soul life is something quite different, also in that case a Noble life is impossible. Both these extremes the Perfect One has avoided and shown the Middle Doctrine, which says: 'On ignorance depend the kammic\-constructions, on the kammic\-constructions depends consciousness', etc.; [S.](dic2-abbrev.htm#S.) XII. 35.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"

summary = "**[]()Jīvita:** and **[]()Jīvi ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Jīvita:** and **[]()Jīvitindriya:** 'Life, vitality', may be either physical [*rūpa*](dic3_r.htm#rūpa) \- *jīvitindriya* or mental *nāma* \- *jīvitindriya* The latter is one of the mental properties inseparably associated with all consciousness; cf. *nāma, cetanā, phassa.*

**[]()Pabbajjā:** lit. 'the going forth', or more fully stated, 'the going forth from home to the homeless life' of a Bhikkhu *agārasmā,* *anagāriyam* consists in severing all family and social ties to live the pure life of a monk, in order to realize the goal of final deliverance pointed out by the Enlightened One. Thus, **p.** has become the name for admission as a *sāmanera* or novice, i.e. as a candidate for the Order of Bhikkhus, or Bhikkhus.

>
>
>
>
> See Going Forth, by Sumana Samanera [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [27/28](../Wheels/wh027.pdf) and  
> Ordination in Theravāda Buddhism [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [56](../Wheels/wh056.pdf).
>
>
>
>

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "paccavekkhana-suddhi"
summary = "**[]()Paccavekkhana\\-suddhi:** ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Paccavekkhana\-suddhi:** 'purity of reflection', is a name for wise consideration in using the 4 requisites allowed to the monk, i.e. robes, food, dwelling, and medicine; [*sīla*](dic3_s.htm#sīla) 4.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "paccavekkhana-ñāna"
summary = "**[]()Paccavekkhana\\-ñāna:** ' ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Paccavekkhana\-ñāna:** 'retrospective knowledge', refers to the recollected mental image obtained in concentration, or to any inner experience just passed, as for instance, any absorption [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna), or any supra\-mundane [path](dic3_m.htm#magga), or fruition of the [path](dic3_m.htm#magga), etc. see: [*ariya\-puggala*](dic3_a.htm#ariya-puggala) As it is said:;At the end of fruitional consciousness, consciousness sinks into the subconscious stream of existence [*bhavanga\-sota*](dic3_b.htm#bhavanga-sota). Then, breaking off the stream of existence, mental directing *manodvārāvajjana* arises at the mind\-door, for the purpose of reviewing the just passed [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) \-moment. Now, as soon as this stage has passed, 7 moments of impulse consciousness [*javana*](dic3_j.htm#javana) \- [*citta*](dic3_c.htm#citta) one after the other, flash up while reviewing the [path](dic3_m.htm#magga). After they again have sunk into the subconscious stream, there arise, for the purpose of reviewing the fruition of the [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) the moments of directing and impulsion, during whose arising the Bhikkhu is reviewing the [path](dic3_m.htm#magga), reviewing the fruition, reviewing the abandoned defilements, reviewing the still remaining defilements, reviewing *[Nibbāna](dic3_n.htm#Nibbāna)* as object. 'This blessing have I attained'. 'This and that defilement still remains in me'. 'This object have I beheld in my mind', etc.; [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XXII.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "paccaya"
summary = "**[]()Paccaya:** 'condition', ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Paccaya:** 'condition', is something on which something else, the so\-called 'conditioned thing', is dependent, and without which the latter cannot be. Many are the ways in which one thing, or one occurrence, may be the condition for some other thing, or occurrence. In the Patthāna, the last book of the Abhidhamma Pitaka comprising 6 large vols. in the Siamese edition, these 24 modes of conditionality are enumerated and explained, and then applied to all conceivable mental and physical phenomena and occurrences, and thus their conditioned nature is demonstrated.

The first two volumes of the Patthāna have been translated into English by the Venerable U Nārada [*mūla*](dic3_m.htm#mūla) patthāna Sayadaw of Burma, under the title Conditional Relations Published by the Pāli Text Society, London 1969, 1981. For a synopsis of this work, see [Guide](dic2-abbrev.htm#Guide) VII.

The 24 modes of conditionality are:

>
>
>
>
> 1. Root condition: [*hetu*](dic3_h.htm#hetu) [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya)  
> 2. Object: [*ārammana*](dic3_a.htm#ārammana)  
> 3. Predominance: [*adhipati*](dic3_a.htm#adhipati)  
> 4. Proximity: *[anantara](dic3_a.htm#anantara-paccaya)*  
> 5. Contiguity: *samanantara*  
> 6. Co\-nascence: *sahajāta*  
> 7. Mutuality: *aññamañña*  
> 8. Support: [*nissaya*](dic3_n.htm#nissaya)  
> 9. Decisive Support: *upanissaya*  
> 10. Pre\-nascene: *purejāta*  
> 11. Post\-nascene: *pacchājāta*  
> 12. Repitition: *āsevana*  
> 13. Kamma: [*kamma*](dic3_k.htm#kamma)  
> 14. Kamma\-result: [*vipāka*](dic3_v.htm#vipāka)  
> 15. Nutriment: [*āhāra*](dic3_a.htm#āhāra)  
> 16. Ability: [*indriya*](dic3_i.htm#indriya)  
> 17. Jhāna: [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna)  
> 18. [path](dic3_m.htm#magga): *[magga](dic3_m.htm#magga)*  
> 19. Associaton: *sampayutta*  
> 20. Dissociation: *vippayutta*  
> 21. Presence: [*atthi*](dic3_a.htm#Atthi-paccaya)  
> 22. Absence: *natthi*  
> 23. Disappearance: *vigata*  
> 24. Non\-disappearance: *[avigata](dic3_a.htm#avigata-paccaya)*
>
>
>
>

1: Root\-condition [*hetu*](dic3_h.htm#hetu) \- [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) is that condition that resembles the root of a tree. Just as a tree rests on its root, and remains alive only as long as its root is not destroyed, similarly all kammically advantageous and disadvantageous mental states are entirely dependent on the simultaneity and presence of their respective roots, i.e, of greed [*lobha*](dic3_l.htm#lobha), hate [*dosa*](dic3_d.htm#dosa) confusion [*moha*](dic3_m.htm#moha) or greedlessness [*alobha*](dic3_a.htm#alobha) hatelessness [*adosa*](dic3_a.htm#adosa) unconfusedness [*amoha*](dic3_a.htm#amoha) For the definition of these 6 roots, see: [*mūla*](dic3_m.htm#mūla)

The roots are a condition by way of root for the mental phenomena associated with a root, and for the material phenomena produced thereby e.g. for bodily expression; Patth.

2: Object\-condition [*ārammana*](dic3_a.htm#ārammana) \- [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) is called something which, as object, forms the condition for consciousness and mental phenomena. Thus, the physical object of sight consisting in colour and light 'light\-wave', is the necessary condition and the sine qua non for the arising of visual\-consciousness [*cakkhu\-viññāna*](dic3_c.htm#cakkhu-viññāna) etc.; sound 'sound wave' for ear\-consciousness *sotā* \- [*viññāna*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna) etc.; further, any object arising in the mind is the condition for mind\-consciousness [*mano*](dic3_m.htm#mano) \- [*viññāna*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna) The mental\-object may be anything whatever, material or mental, past, present or future, real or imaginary.

3: []()Predominance\-condition [*adhipati\-paccaya*](dic3_a.htm#adhipati-paccaya) is the term for 4 things, on the preponderance and predominance of which are dependent the mental phenomena associated with them, namely: concentrated intention [*chanda*](dic3_c.htm#chanda), energy [*viriya*](dic3_v.htm#viriya), consciousness [*citta*](dic3_c.htm#citta) and investigation *vīmamsā* In one and the same state of consciousness, however, only one of these 4 phenomena can be predominant at a time.;Whenever such phenomena as consciousness and mental properties are arising by giving preponderance to one of these 4 things, then this phenomenon is for the other phenomena a condition by way of predominance; [Patth.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Patth.). Cf. [*iddhi\-pāda*](dic3_i.htm#iddhi-pāda)

4\-5: Proximity and contiguity or immediacy\-condition *anantara* and *[samanantara\-paccaya](dic3_s.htm#samanantara-paccaya)* \- both being identical \- refer to any state of consciousness and mental phenomena associated with them, which are the conditions for the immediately following stage in the process of consciousness. For example, in the visual process, visual\-consciousness is for the immediately following mindelement \- performing the function of receiving the visible object \- a condition by way of contiguity; and so is this mind\-element for the next following mind\-consciousness element, performing the function of investigating the object, etc. Cf. [*viññāna\-kicca*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna-kicca).

6: Co\-nascence condjtion [*sahajāta\-paccaya*](dic3_s.htm#sahajāta-paccaya) i.e. condition by way of simultaneous arising, is a phenomenon that for another one forms, a condition in such a way that, simultaneously with its arising, also the other thing must arise. Thus, for instance, in one and the same moment each of the 4 mental groups feeling, perception, mental constructions and consciousness is for the 3 other groups a condition by way of co\-nascence or co\-arising; or again each of the 4 physical elements solid, liquid, heat, motion is such a condition for the other 3 elements. Only at the moment of conception in the mother’s womb does materiality physical base of mind serve for the 4 mental groups as a condition by way of conascence.

7: Condition by way of mutuality [*aññāmañña\-paccaya*](dic3_a.htm#aññāmañña-paccaya) All the just mentioned associated and co\-nascent mental phenomena, as well as the 4 physical elements, are, of course, at the same time also conditioned by way of mutuality,;just like three sticks propped up one by another.; The 4 mental groups are one for another a condition by way of mutuality. So also are the 4 elements, and also mentality and materiality at the moment of conception.

8: Support\-condition [*nissaya\-paccaya*](dic3_n.htm#nissaya-paccaya) This condition refers either to a pre\-nascent see: 10 or co\-nascent see: 6 phenomenon which is aiding other phenomena in the manner of a foundation or base, just as the trees have the earth as their foundation, or as the oil\-painting rests on the canvas. In this way, the 5 sense\-organs and the physical base of the mind are for the corresponding 6 kinds of consciousness a prenascent, i.e. previously arisen, condition by way of support. Further all co\-nascent see: 6 phenomena are mutually see: 7 conditioned by each other by way of support.

9: Decisive\-support or inducement condition [*upanissaya\-paccaya*](dic3_u.htm#upanissaya-paccaya) is threefold, namely a by way of object *ārammanūpanissaya* \- [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) b by way of proximity *anantarūpanissaya* c natural decisive support *pakatupanissaya* These conditions act as strong inducement or cogent reason.

>
>
>
>
> a Anything past, present or future, material or mental, real or imaginary, may, as object of our thinking, become a decisive support, or strong inducement, to moral, immoral or kammically neutral states of mind. Evil things, by wrong thinking about them, become an inducement to immoral life; by right thinking, an inducement to moral life. But good things may be an inducement not only to similarly good things, but also to bad things, such as self\-conceit, vanity, envy, etc.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> b; is identical with proximity condition No. 4.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> c Faith, virtue, etc., produced in one’s own mind, or the influence of climate, food, etc., on one’s body and mind, may act as natural and decisive support\-conditions. Faith may be a direct and natural inducement to charity, virtue to mental training, etc.; greed to theft, hate to murder; unsuitable food and climate to ill\-health; friends to spiritual progress or deterioration.
>
>
>
>

10: Pre\-nascence\-condition [*purejāta\-paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#purejāta-paccaya) refers to something previously arisen, which forms a base for something arising later on. For example, the 5 physical sense\-organs and the physical base of mind, having already arisen at the time of birth, form the condition for the consciousness arising later, and for the mental phenomena associated therewith.

11: Post\-nascence\-condition *pacchā* \- *jāta* \- [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) refers to consciousness and the phenomena therewith associated, because they are \- just as is the feeling of hunger\- a necessary condition for the preservation of this already arisen body.

12: Repetition\-condition [*āsevana\-paccaya*](dic3_a.htm#āsevana-paccaya) refers to the kammical consciousness, in which each time the preceding impulse moments [*javana*](dic3_j.htm#javana) \- [*citta*](dic3_c.htm#citta) are for all the succeeding ones a condition by way of repetition and frequency, just as in learning by heart, through constant repetition, the later recitation becomes gradually easier and easier.

13: Kamma\-condition [*kamma\-paccaya*](dic3_k.htm#kamma-paccaya) The pre\-natal kamma i.e kamma\-intentions, [*kamma*](dic3_k.htm#kamma) \- *[cetanā](dic3_c.htm#cetanā)* in a previous birth is the generating condition cause of the 5 sense\-organs, the fivefold sense\-consciousness, and the other kamma\-produced mental and material phenomena in a later birth. \- Kammical intention is also a condition by way of kamma for the co\-nascent mental phenomena associated therewith, but these phenomena are in no way kamma\-results.

14: Kamma\-result\-condition [*vipāka\-paccaya*](dic3_v.htm#vipāka-paccaya) The kamma\-resultant 5 kinds of sense\-consciousness are a condition by way of kamma\-result for the co\-nascent mental and material phenomena.

15: Nutriment\-condition [*āhāra*](dic3_a.htm#āhāra) \- [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) For the 4 nutriments, see: [*āhāra*](dic3_a.htm#āhāra)

16: Ability\-condition [*indriya\-paccaya*](dic3_i.htm#indriya-paccaya) This condition applies to 20 abilities [*indriya*](dic3_i.htm#indriya), leaving out No. 7 and 8 from the 22 abilities. Of these 20 abilities, the 5 physical sense\-organs 1 \- 5, in their capacity as abilities, form a condition only for unmaterial phenomena visual\-consciousness etc.; physical vitality 6 and all the remaining abilities, for the co\-nascent mental and material phenomena.

17: Jhāna\-condition [*jhāna\-paccaya*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna-paccaya) is a name for the 7 so\-called jhāna\-factors, as these form a condition to the co\-nascent mental and material phenomena, to wit: 1 thought\-conception *vitakka* 2 discursive thinking [*vicāra*](dic3_v.htm#vicāra) 3 interest [*pīti*](dic3_p.htm#pīti) 4 joy [*sukha*](dic3_s.htm#sukha) 5 sadness [*domanassa*](dic3_d.htm#domanassa) 6 indifference *[upekkhā](dic3_u.htm#upekkhā)* 7 concentration [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) For definition s. Pāli terms.

1, 2, 3, 4, 7 are found in 4 classes of greedy consciousness see: [Tab. I](table1.htm). 22\-25; 1, 2, 5, 7 in hateful consciousness ib. 30, 31; 1, 2, 6, 7 in the classes of confused consciousness ib. 32, 33.

This condition does not only apply to [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna) alone, but also to the general intensifying 'absorbing' impact of these 7 factors.

18 [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) \-condition [*magga\-paccaya*](dic3_m.htm#magga-paccaya) refers to the 12 [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) \-factors, as these are for the kammically advantageous and disadvantageous mental phenomena associated with them, a way of escape from this or that mental constitution, namely: 1 knowledge *paññā = sammāditthi* right understanding, 2 right or wrong thought\-conception *vitakka* 3 right speech *sammā* \- *[vācā](dic3_v.htm#vācā)* 4 right bodily action *sammā* \- [*kammanta*](dic3_k.htm#kammanta), 5 right livelihood *sammā* \- *ājīva* 6 right or wrong energy [*viriya*](dic3_v.htm#viriya) 7 right or wrong awareness or mindfulness [*sati*](dic3_s.htm#sati) 8 right or wrong concentration [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) 9 wrong views *micchāditthi* 10 wrong speech *micchā* \- *[vācā](dic3_v.htm#vācā)* 11 wrong bodily action *micchā* \- [*kammanta*](dic3_k.htm#kammanta) 12 wrong livelihood *micchā* \- *ājīva* Cf. [*magga*](dic3_m.htm#magga)

19: Association\-condition [*sampayutta\-paccaya*](dic3_s.htm#sampayutta-paccaya) refers to the co\-nascent see: 6 and mutually see: 7 conditioned 4 mental groups [*khandha*](dic3_k.htm#khandha) as they aid each other by their being associated, by having a common physical base, a common object, and by their arising and disappearing simultaneously; [Patth.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Patth.) [Com.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Com.).

20: Dissociation\-condition [*vippayutta\-paccaya*](dic3_v.htm#vippayutta-paccaya) refers to such phenomena as aid other phenomena by not baving the same physical base eye, etc. and objects. Thus material phenomena are for mental phenomena, and conversely, a condition by way of dissociation, whether co\-nascent or not.

21: Presence\-condition *atthi* \- [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) refers to a phenomenon \- being pre\-nascent or co\-nascent \- which through its presence is a condition for other phenomena. This condition applies to the conditions Nos. 6, 7, 8, 10, 11.

22: Absence\-condition [*natthi\-paccaya*](dic3_n.htm#natthi-paccaya) refers to consciousness, etc., which has just passed, and which thus forms the necessary condition for the immediately following stage of consciousness by giving it an opportunity to arise. Cf. No. 4.

23: Disappearance\-condition [*vigata\-paccaya*](dic3_v.htm#vigata-paccaya) is identical with No. 22.

24: Non\-disappearance\-condition [*avigata\-paccaya*](dic3_a.htm#avigata-paccaya) is identical with No. 21.

These 24 conditions should be known thoroughly for a detailed understanding of that famous formula of the dependent origination [*paticcasamuppāda*](dic3_p.htm#paticcasamuppāda). Cf. [Fund.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Fund.) III, [Guide](dic2-abbrev.htm#Guide) p. 117 ff. [App.](dic2-abbrev.htm#App.).

>
>
>
>
> See The Significance of Dependent Origination, by Nyanatiloka [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [140](../Wheels/wh394.pdf).
>
>
>
>

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
```
``` toml
word = "pacceka-buddha"
summary = "**[]()Pacceka\\-buddha:** an 'S ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Pacceka\-buddha:** an 'Solitarily Enlightened One'; or Separately or Individually = *pacceka* Enlightened One renderings by 'Silent' or 'Private Buddha' are not very apt. This is a term for an Arahat see: [*ariya\-puggala*](dic3_a.htm#ariya-puggala) who has realized *[Nibbāna](dic3_n.htm#Nibbāna)* without having heard the Buddha’s doctrine from others. He comprehends the 4 Noble Truths individually *pacceka* independent of any teacher, by his own effort. He has, however, not the capacity to proclaim the Teaching effectively to others, and therefore does not become a 'Teacher of Gods and Men', a Perfect or Universal [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) *sammā* \- *sambuddha.* Paccekabuddhas are described as frugal of speech, cherishing solitude. According to tradition, they do not arise while the Teaching of a Perfect [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) is known; but for achieving their rank after many aeons of effort, they have to utter an aspiration before a Perfect Buddha.

Canonical references are few; [Pug.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Pug.) 29 defin.; [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) II, 56; in [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 116, names of many Paccekabuddhas are given; in [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 16 they are said to be worthy of a *thūpa* *dagoba;* the Treasure\-Store Sutta Nidhikhandha Sutta, [Khp.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Khp.) mentions [*pacceka\-bodhi*](dic3_p.htm#pacceka-bodhi) the C. Nidd. ascribes to individual Paccekabuddhas the verses of the Rhinoceros Sutta Khaggavisāna Sutta, [Sn.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Sn.) \- See *bodhi.*

>
>
>
>
> See The Paccekabuddha, by Ria Kloppenborg [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [305/307](../Wheels/wh305.pdf).
>
>
>
>
