**[[pānātipātā veramanī]]Pānātipātā veramanī:** 'abstaining from the killing of living beings', is the first of the 5 moral rules binding upon all Buddhists; see: [*sikkhāpada*](dic3_s.htm#sikkhāpada)

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "pārisuddhi-padhāniyanga"
summary = "**[]()Pārisuddhi\\-padhāniyanga ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Pārisuddhi\-padhāniyanga:** the 4 'elements of the effort for purity', are: effort for purity of morality [*sīla*](dic3_s.htm#sīla) \- *parisuddhi* \- *[padhāniyanga](dic3_p.htm#padhāniyanga)* for purity of mind [*citta*](dic3_c.htm#citta) of view [*ditthi*](dic3_d.htm#ditthi) of deliverance [*vimutti*](dic3_v.htm#vimutti) Cf. [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) IV, 194. \- Another 9 factors are enumerated in [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 34, namely the 7 'stages of purification see: [*visuddhi*](dic3_v.htm#visuddhi) and the effort for purity of higher knowledge *[vijjā](dic3_v.htm#vijjā)* \- *p. p* and of deliverance [*vimutti*](dic3_v.htm#vimutti) \- *p. p.* .

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "pārisuddhi-sīla"
summary = "**[]()Pārisuddhi\\-sīla:** 'mor ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Pārisuddhi\-sīla:** 'morality consisting in purity', is fourfold: restraint with regard to the Bhikkhus' Disciplinary Code, sense restraint, purity of livelihood, morality with regard to the Bhikkhus' 4 requisites; for details, see: [*sīla*](dic3_s.htm#sīla)

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "pātihāriya"
summary = "**[]()Pātihāriya:** 'miracle', ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Pātihāriya:** 'miracle', marvel. Three marvels are ascribed to the Buddha: the marvel of magic [*iddhi*](dic3_i.htm#iddhi) \- *p* the marvel of mind\-reading *ādesanā* \- *p* and the marvel of instruction *anusāsanī* \- *p* In [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 11, the [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) says that he sees danger in the first two and therefore abhors them. In [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) III, 61, the 'marvel of instruction' is called the one 'more noble and sublime'. For iddhi\-pātihāriya, see [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 25. See also *yamakapātihāriya.*

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "pātimokkha"
summary = "**[]()Pātimokkha:** 'Disciplin ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Pātimokkha:** 'Disciplinary Code', is the name of the code of monk’s rules, which on all full\-moon and new moon days is recited before the assembled community of fully ordained Bhikkhus [*Bhikkhu*](dic3_b.htm#bhikkhu).

**[]()Pātimokkha\-samvara\-sīla:** 'morality consisting in restraint with regard to the Disciplinary Code' *[pātimokkha](dic3_p.htm#pātimokkha)* see: prec.. For details, see: [*sīla*](dic3_s.htm#sīla).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
```
``` toml
word = "pīti"
summary = "**[]()Pīti:** rapture, enthusi ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Pīti:** rapture, enthusiasm rendered also by joy, happiness; interest it is one of the mental properties or properties [*cetasika*](dic3_c.htm#cetasika) and belongs to the group of mental constructions [*sankhāra*](dic3_s.htm#sankhāra) \- *[khandha](dic3_k.htm#khandha)* As, in sutta texts, it is often linked in a compound word. with 'gladness' *pāmojja* or 'happiness' [*sukha*](dic3_s.htm#sukha) some Western translations have wrongly taken it as a synonym of these two terms. Pīti, however, is not a feeling or a sensation, and hence does not belong to the feeling\-group *[vedanā](dic3_v.htm#vedanā)* \- *[khandha](dic3_k.htm#khandha),* but may be described psychologically as 'joyful interest'. As such it may be associated with advantageous as well as with disadvantageous and neutral states of consciousness.

A high degree of rapture is characteristic of certain stages in meditative concentration, in insight practice *[vipassanā](dic3_v.htm#vipassanā)* as well as in the first two absorptions [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna). In the latter it appears as one of the factors of absorption [*jhānanga*](dic3_j.htm#jhānanga) see: [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna) and is strongest in the 2nd absorption. Five degrees of intensity in meditative rapture are described in [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) IV. 94ff. It is one of the factors of enlightenment [*bojjhanga*](dic3_b.htm#bojjhanga).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "pūjā"
summary = "**[]()Pūjā:** 1 honour, respec ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Pūjā:** 1 honour, respect, homage, 2 worship, devotional observances, devotional offerings; also offerings to Bhikkhus.

1: The Mahā\-mangala Sutta [Sn.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Sn.) 259 says that;Honour and respect towards those worthy of it, is conducive to great blessing; *pūjā ca pūjaniyesu etam mangalam uttamarn* See [Dhp.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Dhp.) 195f.

2: The [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) did not think much of mere outer worship.;Not thus, Ananda, is the Tathāgata respected, venerated, esteemed, worshipped and honoured in the highest degree. But, Ananda, whatsoever Bhikkhu or Bhikkhuni, lay man or lay woman, abides by the Teaching, lives uprightly in the Teaching, walks in the way of the Teaching, it is by him that the Tathāgata is respected, venerated, esteemed, worshipped and honoured in the highest degree; [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 16. \-;There are two kinds of worship: in a material way *āmisa* \- *[pūjā](dic3_p.htm#pūjā)* and through practice of the Dhamma [*dhamma*](dic3_d.htm#dhamma) \- *[pūjā](dic3_p.htm#pūjā)* The worship through practice of the Dhamma is the better of the two; [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) II.

**[]()Tadanga\-pahāna:** 'overcoming by the opposite', is one of the 5 kinds of overcoming [*pahāna*](dic3_p.htm#pahāna),.

**[]()Tadārammana\-citta:** 'registering consciousness' see: [Tab. I](table1.htm), 40\-49, 56, is the last stage in the complete process of cognition citta\-vīthi immediately before sinking into the subconscious. It does not occur with the consciousness of the absorptions nor with supra\-mundane consciousness, but only with large or distinct objects of the sense\-sphere. Cf. [*viññāna\-kicca*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna-kicca).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
```
``` toml
word = "tanhā"
summary = "**[]()Tanhā:** lit. 'thirst': ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Tanhā:** lit. 'thirst': 'craving', is the chief root of suffering, and of the ever\-continuing cycle of rebirths.;What, o Bhikkhus, is the origin of suffering? It is that craving which gives rise to ever\-fresh rebirth and, bound up with pleasure and lust, now here, now there, finds ever fresh delight. It is the sensual craving [*kāma\-tanhā*](dic3_k.htm#kāma-tanhā) the craving for existence [*bhava\-tanhā*](dic3_b.htm#bhava-tanhā) the craving for non\-existence *vibhava* \- *[tanhā](dic3_t.htm#tanhā)* [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 22. **T.** is the 8th link in the formula of the dependent origination [*paticcasamuppāda*](dic3_p.htm#paticcasamuppāda). Cf. [*sacca*](dic3_s.htm#sacca).

Corresponding to the 6 sense\-objects, there are 6 kinds of craving craving for visible objects, for sounds, odours, tastes, bodily contacts, mental contacts *rūpa\-, sadda\-, gandha\-, rasa\-, photthabba\-, dhamma\-tanhā* [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 9; [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 15

Corresponding to the 3\-fold existence, there are 3 kinds: craving for sensual existence [*kāma\-tanhā*](dic3_k.htm#kāma-tanhā) for fine\-material existence [*rūpa*](dic3_r.htm#rūpa) \- *[tanhā](dic3_t.htm#tanhā)* for immaterial existence *arūpa* \- *[tanhā](dic3_t.htm#tanhā)* [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 33

There are 18 'thought\-channels of craving' *[tanhā](dic3_t.htm#tanhā)* \- *vicarita* induced internally, and 18 induced externally; and as occurring in past, present and future, they total 108; see [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) IV, 199; [Vibh.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vibh.), Ch. 17 Khuddakavatthu\-Vibhanga.

According to the dependent origination, craving is conditioned by feeling; on this see [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 22 section on the 2nd Truth.

Of craving for existence [*bhava\-tanhā*](dic3_b.htm#bhava-tanhā) it is said [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) X, 62:;No first beginning of the craving for existence can be perceived, o Bhikkhus, before which it was not and after which it came to be. But it can he perceived that craving for existence has its specific condition. I say, o Bhikkhus, that also craving for existence has its condition that feeds it *sāharam* and is not without it. And what is it? 'Ignorance', one has to reply.; \- Craving for existence and ignorance are called;the outstanding causes that lead to happy and unhappy destinies courses of existence; see: [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XVII, 36\-42.

The most frequent synonyms of *[tanhā](dic3_t.htm#tanhā)* are [*rāga*](dic3_r.htm#rāga) and [*lobha*](dic3_l.htm#lobha) see: [*mūla*](dic3_m.htm#mūla).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"

summary = "**[]()Tanhā\\-kkhaya:** 'ceasin ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Tanhā\-kkhaya:** 'ceasing of craving', is identical with 'ceasing of fermentations' [*āsavakkhaya*](dic3_a.htm#āsavakkhaya) and the attainment of perfect Nobility or Arahatship. Cf. [*ariya\-puggala*](dic3_a.htm#ariya-puggala).


**[]()Tanhā\-nissita\-sīla:** 'morality based on craving' see: [*nissaya*](dic3_n.htm#nissaya).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "tathatā"
summary = "**[]()Tathatā:** 'Suchness', d ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Tathatā:** 'Suchness', designates the firmly fixed nature [*bhāva*](dic3_b.htm#bhāva) of all things whatever. The only passage in the Canon where the word occurs in this sense, is found in [Kath.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Kath.) 186 see: [Guide](dic2-abbrev.htm#Guide), p. 83. On the Mahāyana term *[tathatā](dic3_t.htm#tathatā)* see: Suzuki, Awakening of Faith, p. 53f. [App.](dic2-abbrev.htm#App.).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "tathāgata"
summary = "**[]()Tathāgata:** the 'Perfec ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Tathāgata:** the 'Perfect One', lit. the one who has 'thus gone', or 'thus come', is an epithet of the [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) used by him when speaking of himself.

To the often asked questions, whether the Tathāgata still exists after death, or not, it is said e.g. [S.](dic2-abbrev.htm#S.) XXII, 85, 86 that, in the highest sense [*paramattha*](dic3_p.htm#paramattha) the Tathāgata cannot, even at lifetime, be discovered, how much less after death, and that neither the 5 groups of existence [*khandha*](dic3_k.htm#khandha) are to be regarded as the Tathāgata, nor can the Tathāgata be found outside these material and mental phenomena. The meaning intended here is that there exist only these ever\-changing material and mental phenomena, arising and vanishing from moment to moment, but no separate entity, no personality.

When the commentaries in this connection explain Tathāgata by 'living being' [*satta*](dic3_s.htm#satta) they mean to say that here the questioners are using the merely conventional expression, Tathāgata, in the sense of a really existing entity.

Cf. *anattā, paramattha, puggala, jīva, satta.*

>
>
>
>
> A commentarial treatise on;The Meaning of the Word 'Tathāgata’is included in The All\-Embracing Net of Views Brahmajāla Sutta, tr. Bhikkhu Bodhi [BPS](dic2-abbrev.htm#BPS).
>
>
>
>

**[]()Tatra\-majjhattatā:** 'equanimity, equipoise, mental balance' lit., 'remaining here and there in the middle', is the name for a high ethical quality belonging to the [*sankhāra*](dic3_s.htm#sankhāra) \- *[khandha](dic3_k.htm#khandha)* see: [*khandha*](dic3_k.htm#khandha) and is mostly known by the name *[upekkhā](dic3_u.htm#upekkhā)* In its widest sense it is associated with all pure consciousness see: [Tab. II.](table2.htm). *tatra* \- *majjhattatā* is called the 'keeping in the middle of all things'. It has as charactcristic that it effects the balance of consciousness and mental properties; as nature function; *rasa* that it prevents excessiveness and deficiency, or that it puts an end to partiality; as manifestation, that it keeps the proper middle; [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XIV. [App.](dic2-abbrev.htm#App.).

**[]()Te\-vijja:** 'one endowed with the threefold higher knowledge'. In Brahmanism means 'knower of the 3 Vedas' *tri* \- *vidyā* in Buddhism means one who has realised 3 kinds of knowledge, to wit: remembrance of former rebirths, the divine eye, ceasing of all fermentations. For details, see: [*abhiññā*](dic3_a.htm#abhiññā) 4\-6. Cf. Tevijjā Sutta, [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 13 [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [57/58](../Wheels/wh057.pdf).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
```

``` toml
summary = "**[]()Theravāda:** 'Doctrine o ..."

```

**[]()Theravāda:** 'Doctrine of the Elders', is a name of the oldest form of the Buddha’s teachings, handed down to us in the Pāli language. According to tradition, its name is derived from the fact of having been fixed by 500 Noble Elders of the Order, soon after the death of the Master.

Theravāda is the only one of the old schools of Buddhism that has survived among those which Mahāyānists have called 'Hinayāna'. It is sometimes called Southern Buddhism or Pāli Buddhism. It is found today in Sri Lanka, Burma, Thailand, Cambodia, Laos and Chittagong East Bengal. \- Cf. [Guide](dic2-abbrev.htm#Guide), p. 60. \- [App.](dic2-abbrev.htm#App.).

**[]()Thinking:** understanding based on: *cintāmayapaññā* see: *[paññā](dic3_p.htm#paññā).*

**[]()Thīna\-middha:** 'lethargy and Laziness' or 'lethargy and laziness', constitute the 3rd of the 5 hindrances [*nīvarana*](dic3_n.htm#nīvarana). They may or may not, be associated with greedy consciousness see: [Tab.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Tab.) 23. 25, 27, 29 and II.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
```
``` toml
word = "ti-lakkhana"
summary = "**[]()Ti\\-lakkhana:** the '3 c ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Ti\-lakkhana:** the '3 charactcristies of existence', or signata, are impermanency [*anicca*](dic3_a.htm#anicca), suffcring or [misery](dic3_d.htm#dukkha) [*dukkha*](dic3_d.htm#dukkha) see: *sacca, dukkhatā* no\-self [*anattā*](dic3_a.htm#anattā).

Whether Perfect Ones appear in the world, or whether Perfect Ones do not appear in the world, it still remains a firm condition, an immutable fact and fixed law: that all constructions are impermanent, that all constructions are subject to suffering, that everything is without a self'' [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) III, 134.

What do you think, o Bhikkhus: Is materiality [*rūpa*](dic3_r.htm#rūpa) permanent or impermanent? \- Impermanent, o Venerable One. \- Are feeling [*vedanā*](dic3_v.htm#vedanā) perception *[saññā](dic3_s.htm#saññā)* mental constructions [*sankhāra*](dic3_s.htm#sankhāra) and consciousness [*viññāna*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna) permanent or impermanent? \- Impermanent, o Venerable One.

But that which is impermanent, is it something pleasant or painful? \- It is painful, o Venerable One.

But, of what is impermanent, painful and subject to change, could it be rightly said, 'This belongs to me, this am I, this is my ego'? \- No, Venerable One.

'I’herefore, whatever there is of materiality, feeling, perception, mental constructions and consciousness, whether past, present or future, one’s own or external, gross or subtle, lofty or low, far or near, of all these things one should understand, according to reality and true understanding: 'This does not belong to me, this am I not, this is not my ego' [S.](dic2-abbrev.htm#S.) XXII, 59.

In one who understands eye, ear, nose, tongue, body and all the remaining constructions as impermanent, painful and no\-self, in him the mental chains [*samyojana*](dic3_s.htm#samyojana) are dissolved; [S.](dic2-abbrev.htm#S.) XXXV, 53.

It is the full comprehension of the 3 characteristics by direct meditative experience which constitutes liberating insight. About their relation to the three gateways ot liberation', see: [*vimokkha*](dic3_v.htm#vimokkha) I.

For further details, see: *anicca, dukkha, anattā, vipassanā.*

>
>
>
>
> Literature: The Three Signata, by Prof. O. H. de [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) Wijesekera [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [20](../Wheels/wh020.pdf). \- The Three Basic Facts of Existence: I\-III [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [BPS](dic2-abbrev.htm#BPS), [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XX, 13ff. 18ff; XXI, 47f, 67f.
>

**[]()Ti\-pitaka:** ' The Three Baskets', is the name for the 3 main divisions of the Pāli Canon: the Basket of Discipline Vinaya Pitaka, the Basket of Discourses Sutta Pitaka and the Basket ot Philosophy Abhidhamma Pitaka.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "ti-ratana"
summary = "**[]()Ti\\-ratana:** 'Three Jew ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Ti\-ratana:** 'Three Jewels' or Three Gems, which by all Buddhists are revered as the most venerable things, are the Buddha, the Dhamma and the Noble Sangha.' i.e.: the Enlightened One; the law of deliverance discovered, realized and proclaimed by him; and the Community of Noble Disciples and those who live in accordance with the Law. \- The contemplations of the 3 Jewels belong to the 10 contemplations [*anussati*](dic3_a.htm#anussati).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "ti-sarana"
summary = "**[]()Ti\\-sarana:** 'Threefold ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Ti\-sarana:** 'Threefold Refuge', in which every faithful adherent of the [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) puts his whole trust, consists in the Buddha, the Dhamma and the Sangha see: prec..

The Buddha, or Enlightened One, is the teacher who by himself has discovered, realized and proclaimed to the world the law of deliverance. The Dhamma is the law of deliverance. The Sangha is the community of the disciples, who have realized or are striving to realize the law of deliverance.

The 3\-fold Refuge in Pāli, by the uttering of which one may also outwardly profess one’s faith, is still the same as in the Buddha’s time, namely:

>
>
>
>
> Buddham saranam gacchāmi  
> Dhammam saranam gacchāmi  
> Sangham saranam gacchāmi
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> I take refuge in the Buddha!  
> I take refuge in the Dhamma!  
> I take refuge in the Sangha!
>
>
>
>

Literature: The Threefold Refuge by Nyanaponika Thera [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [76](../Wheels/wh076.pdf). \- Devotion in Buddhism [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [18](../Wheels/wh018.pdf). Going for Refuge, by Bhikkhu Bodhi [WHEEL](dic2-abbrev.htm#WHEEL) [282/284](../Wheels/wh282.pdf) \- [Khp.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Khp.) Tr. pp. 4ff.

**[]()Tiracchāna\-kathā:** 'low talk', lit. 'beastly talk', is the name in the sutta\-texts for the following:;Talk about kings and robbers, ministers and armies, danger and war, eating and drinking, clothes and dwellings, garlands and scents, relations, chariots, villages and markets, towns and districts, women and heroes, street talks, talks by the well, talk about those departed in days gone by, tittle\-tattle, talks about world and sea, about gain and loss; [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) X, 69 etc..

In the commentaries 4 further kinds are enumerated, thus bringing the number to 32, as mostly counted, namely: talk about sense\-enjoyment, self\-mortification, eternity and self\-annihilation.

**[]()Tiracchāna\-yoni:** 'animal womb'; birth as animal. The animal kingdom belongs to the sense\-world see: [*loka*](dic3_l.htm#loka) is one of the 4 lower worlds see: [*apāya*](dic3_a.htm#apāya) and one of the 3 woeful courses of existence see: [*gati*](dic3_g.htm#gati)

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "titthāyatana"
summary = "**[]()Titthāyatana:** the 3 'a ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Titthāyatana:** the 3 'articles of heretical belief'. which in [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) III, 61 are declared as leading to inactivity, are: 1 the belief that all happiness and woe are produced through former kamma prenatal actions; see: kamma; 2 that everything is uncaused; 3 that everything is created by God.

1 is the teaching of Niggantha\-Nāthaputta, the leader of the Nigganthas, the modern Jains. The fault with this doctrine is that it does not account for that happiness and woe which either are the result of the present life’s good or bad action, or are associated with the corresponding action. 2 is the doctrine of Makkhali Gosāla; see: [*ditthi*](dic3_d.htm#ditthi)

According to the above 3 doctrines, man is not responsible for his actions, so that all moral exertions become useless.


**[]()Ādibrahmacariyaka\-sīla:** 'morality of genuine pure conduct', consists in right speech, right bodily action and right livelihood, forming the 3rd, 4th and 5th links of the 8\-fold [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) see: [*sacca*](dic3_s.htm#sacca) IV.3, 4, 5; cf. [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) I. In [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) II, 86 it is said:

With regard to those moral states connected with and corresponding to the genuine pure conduct, he is morally strong, morally firm and trains himself in the moral rules taken up by himself. After overcoming the 3 mental chains ego\-belief, skeptic doubt and attachment to mere rules and ritual; see: [*samyojana*](dic3_s.htm#samyojana) he becomes one who will be 'reborn 7 times at most' see: *[sotāpanna](dic3_s.htm#sotāpanna)* and after only seven times more wandering through this round of rebirths amongst men and divine beings, he will put an end to suffering.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "ādīnavānupassanā-ñāna"
summary = "**[]()Ādīnavānupassanā\\-ñāna:* ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Ādīnavānupassanā\-ñāna:** 'knowledge consisting in contemplation of danger', is one of the 8 kinds of insight [*vipassanā*](dic3_v.htm#vipassanā) that form the 'purification of the knowledge and vision of the [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) \-progress see: [*visuddhi*](dic3_v.htm#visuddhi) VI. 4. It is further one of the 18 chief kinds of insight see: [*vipassanā*](dic3_v.htm#vipassanā).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "āhāra"
summary = "**[]()Āhāra:** 'nutriment', 'f ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Āhāra:** 'nutriment', 'food', is used in the concrete sense as material food and as such it belongs to derived materiality see: [*khandha*](dic3_k.htm#khandha) Summary I. In the figurative sense, as 'foundation' or sustaining condition, it is one of the 24 conditions [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya) and is used to denote 4 kinds of nutriment, which are material and mental: 1: material food [*kabalinkārāhāra*](dic3_k.htm#kabalinkārāhāra), 2: sensorial and mental contact [*phassa*](dic3_p.htm#phassa), 3: mental intention [*mano*](dic3_m.htm#mano) \- *[sañcetanā](dic3_s.htm#sañcetanā),* 4: consciousness [*viññāna*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna).

1: Material food feeds the 8\-fold materiality having nutrient essence as its 8th factor i.e. the solid, liquid, heat, motion, color, odour, the tastable and nutrient essence; see: [*rūpa\-kalāpa*](dic3_r.htm#rūpa-kalāpa). 2: Sensorial and mental contact is a condition for the 3 kinds of feeling pleasant, painful and indifferent; see: [*paticcasamuppāda*](dic3_p.htm#paticcasamuppāda) 6. 3: Mental intention = kamma feeds rebirth; see: [*paticca* \- *samuppāda*](dic3_p.htm#paticcasamuppāda) 2. 4: Consciousness feeds mind and materiality, *[nāma\-rūpa](dic3_n.htm#nāma-rūpa)* at the moment of conception [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XI.

>
>
>
>
> Literature on the 4 Nutriments: [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 9 & [Com.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Com.) tr. in ' [R. Und.](dic2-abbrev.htm#R.%20Und.) ', [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 38; see: [S.](dic2-abbrev.htm#S.) XII, 11, 63, 64 \- The Four Nutriments of Life, Selected texts & [Com.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Com.) WHEEL [105](../Wheels/wh105.pdf)
>
>
>
>

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
```
``` toml
word = "ākāsa"
summary = "**[]()Ākāsa:** 'space', is, ac ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Ākāsa:** 'space', is, according to [Com.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Com.), of two kinds: 1. limited space *paricchinnākāsa* or *paricchedākāsa,* 2. endless space *anantākāsa,* i.e. cosmic space.

>
>
>
>
> 1. Limited space, under the name of [*ākāsa*](dic3_a.htm#ākāsa) \- [*dhātu*](dic3_d.htm#dhātu) space element, belongs to derived materiality see: [*khandha*](dic3_k.htm#khandha) Summary I; [Dhs](dic2-abbrev.htm#Dhs.). 638 and to a sixfold classification of elements see: [*dhātu*](dic3_d.htm#dhātu) [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 112, 115, 140. It is also an object of kasina meditation. It is defined as follows: The space element has the characteristic of delimiting matter or form. Its function is to indicate the boundaries of matter. It is manifested as the confines and container of matter or form; or its manifestation consists in being untouched by the 4 great elements, and in holes and openings. Its proximate cause is the matter delimited. It is on account of the space element that one can say of material things delimited that 'this is above. below, around that' [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XIV, 63.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 2. Endless space is in [Atthasālini](dic2-abbrev.htm#Atthasālini) called *ajatākāsa* unentangled', i.e. unobstructed or empty space. It is the object of the first formless absorption see: [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna), the sphere of Infinite space [*ākāsānañcāyatana*](dic3_a.htm#ākāsānañcāyatana). According to Abhidhamma philosophy, endless space has no objective reality being purely conceptual, which is indicated by the fact that it is not included in the triad of the advantageous *kusalatika,* which comprises the entire reality. Later Buddhist schools have regarded it as one of several unconditioned or uncreated states [*asankhata*](dic3_a.htm#asankhata) *dharma* \- a view that is rejected in [Kath.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Kath.) see: [Guide](dic2-abbrev.htm#Guide). p. 70. Theravāda Buddhism recognizes only *[Nibbāna](dic3_n.htm#Nibbāna)* as an unconditioned element [*asankhata*](dic3_a.htm#asankhata) [*dhātu*](dic3_d.htm#dhātu) see: [Dhs.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Dhs.) 1084.
>
>
>
>

**[]()Āloka\-kasina:** L ight\-kasina\-meditation on bright light or the white color; see: [*kasina*](dic3_k.htm#kasina)

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "āloka-saññā"
summary = "**[]()Āloka\\-saññā:** Percepti ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Āloka\-saññā:** Perception of light. The recurring canonical passage reads: Here the Bhikkhu contemplates the perception of light. He fixes his\-mind to the experience of the daylight; as at day\-time so at night, and as at night, so in the day. In this way, with a clear and unclouded mind, he develops the stage of mind that is full of brightness. It is one of the methods of overcoming drowsiness, recommended by the [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) to [Mahā\-Moggallāna](../DPPN/maha/maha_moggallana_th.htm) [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) VII, 58. According to [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 33, it is conducive to the development of 'knowledge and vision' see: *[visuddhi](dic3_v.htm#visuddhi) [VI](dic3_v.htm#Visuddhi_VI) \+ [VII](dic3_v.htm#Visuddhi_VII),* and it is said to be helpful to the attainment of the 'divine eye' see: *[abhiññā](dic3_a.htm#abhiññā) [5](#Abhiññā_5).*

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "ānantarika-kamma"
summary = "**[]()Ānantarika\\-kamma:** the ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Ānantarika\-kamma:** the 5 heinous 'actions with immediate destiny' are: Killing father, killing mother, killing an Arahat, wounding a Buddha so he bleeds, creating schism in the Bhikkhu\-Sangha. In [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) V., 129 it is said:

There are 5 hateful and incurable humans destined to the lower world and to hell, namely: the parricide, etc. About the 5th see [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) X., 35, 38. With regard to the first crime, it is said in [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 2 that if [King Ajātasattu](../DPPN/am/ajatasattu.htm) had not killed his father, he would have reached entrance into the [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) of [Stream\-entry](dic3_s.htm#stream-entry) see also: [Appendix.](dic4_append.htm#ānantarika-kamma)

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "ānantariya"
summary = "**[]()Ānantariya:** Immediacy, ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Ānantariya:** Immediacy, is a name for that concentration of mind which is associated with the profound and shocking insight [*vipassanā*](dic3_v.htm#vipassanā) that is present in any one of the 4 kinds of supra\-mundane [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) consciousness see: [*ariya\-puggala*](dic3_a.htm#ariya-puggala), and which therefore is the cause of the immediately following fruition *[phala](dic3_p.htm#phala)* consciousness. According to the Abhidhamma, this [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) \-moment of the *Stream\-enterer [sotāpanna](dic3_s.htm#sotāpanna)* & the other Nobles is generated by the insight into the [impermanence](dic3_a.htm#anicca), [misery](dic3_d.htm#dukkha) and [impersonality](dic3_a.htm#anattā) of all existence, reaching a certain threshold at that very moment and thus instantly transforming and ennobling the individual nature forever. It is mentioned under the name of *ānantarika* \- [*samādhi*](dic3_s.htm#samādhi) in the Ratana Sutta [Sn.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Sn.) v. 22 and in [Pts.M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Pts.M.) 1, ñānakathā.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "āneñja"
summary = "**[]()Āneñja:** Static impertu ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Āneñja:** Static imperturbability, denotes the mental state of being(s) in the formless sphere [*arūpāvacara*](dic3_a.htm#arūpāvacara) [*avacara*](dic3_a.htm#avacara), see: [*sankhāra*](dic3_s.htm#sankhāra) cf. [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 106.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "ānupubbī-kathā"
summary = "**[]()Ānupubbī\\-kathā:** 'grad ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Ānupubbī\-kathā:** 'gradual instruction', progressive teaching; given by the [Buddha](../DPPN/b/buddha.htm) when it was necessary to first prepare the listener’s mind before speaking to him on the advanced teaching of the Four Noble Truths. The stock passage e.g. [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 3; D 14; [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 56 runs as follows:  
Then the Blessed One gave him a gradual instruction \- that is to say, he spoke on generosity [*dāna*](dic3_d.htm#dāna), on morality [*sīla*](dic3_s.htm#sīla) and on the heavens [*sagga*](dic3_s.htm#sagga), he explained the danger, the loss and the depravity of sensual pleasures, and the advantage of renunciation. When the Blessed One perceived that the listener’s mind was prepared, pliant, free from obstacles, elevated and lucid; then he explained to him that exalted teaching particular to the Buddhas *Buddhānam* *sāmukkamsikā,* that is: Suffering, its cause, its ceasing, and the path.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "ānāpāna-sati"
summary = "**[]()Ānāpāna\\-sati:** Awarene ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Ānāpāna\-sati:** Awareness or mindfulness on & by in\-and\-out\-breathing, is one of the most important trainings for reaching mental concentration and the 4 absorptions [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna). In the Satipatthāna Sutta [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 10, [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 22 and elsewhere, 4 methods of practice are given, which may also serve as basis for insight meditation. The speech on Awareness by Breathing' Ānāpānasati Sutta, [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 118 and other texts have 16 methods of practice, which divide into 4 groups of four. The first three apply to both calm [*samatha*](dic3_s.htm#samatha) and insight\-meditation, while the fourth refers to pure insight praxis only. With attentive mind he breathes in, with attentive mind he breathes out.

>
>
>
>
> I. First Tetrad:  
> 1: When making a long inhalation he understands: I make a long inhalation; when making a long exhalation he understands: I make a long exhalation.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 2: When making a short inhalation he understands: I make a short inhalation; when making a short exhalation he understands: I make a short exhalation.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 3: Clearly perceiving the entire body I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; clearly perceiving the entire breath\-body I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 4: Calming all bodily activity I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; calming all bodily activity I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> II. Second Tetrad:  
> 5: Experiencing joy [*pīti*](dic3_p.htm#pīti) I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; Experiencing joy I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 6: Experiencing a pleasurable happiness I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; Experiencing a pleasurable happiness I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 7: Experiencing the mental construction [*citta\-sankhāra*](dic3_c.htm#citta-sankhāra) I will breathe in, thus he trains himself, Experiencing the mental construction I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 8: Calming the mental construction I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; calming the mental construction I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> III. Third Tetrad:  
> 9: Experiencing the mind & mood [*citta*](dic3_c.htm#citta) I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; clearly perceiving the mind & mood I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 10: Gladdening the mind I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; gladdening the mind I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 11: Concentrating the mind I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; concentrating the mind I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 12: Releasing the mind I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; releasing the mind I will breathe out, thus he trains himself
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> IV. Fourth Tetrad:  
> 13: Reflecting on [impermanence](dic3_a.htm#anicca) [*anicca*](dic3_a.htm#anicca) I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; reflecting on [impermanence](dic3_a.htm#anicca) I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 14: Reflecting on disillusion *[virāga](dic3_v.htm#virāga)* I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; reflecting on disillusion I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 15: Reflecting on ceasing [*nirodha*](dic3_n.htm#nirodha) I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; reflecting on ceasing I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>
>
>
>
> 16: Reflecting on relinquishment *[patinissagga](dic3_p.htm#patinissaggānupassanā)* I will breathe in, thus he trains himself; reflecting on relinquishment I will breathe out, thus he trains himself.
>
>
>
>

In M 118 it is further shown how these 16 exercises bring about the 4 foundations of awareness [*satipatthāna*](dic3_s.htm#satipatthāna), namely: 1\-4 contemplation of the body, 5\-8 contemplation of feeling, 9\-12 contemplation of mind, 13\-16 contemplation of mental states. Then it is shown how these 4 foundations of awareness or mindfulness bring about the 7 factors of enlightenment [*bojjhanga*](dic3_b.htm#bojjhanga), and then how these again produce release of mind [*ceto\-vimutti*](dic3_c.htm#ceto-vimutti) and release through understanding [*paññā\-vimutti*](dic3_p.htm#paññā-vimutti).

>
>
>
>
> Literature: Ānāpānasati Samyutta see: LIV. \- [Pts.M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Pts.M.) *Ānāpānakathā* \- Full explanation of practice in [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) VIII, 145ff. \- For a comprehensive anthology of canonical and commentarial texts, see: *[Mindfulness of Breathing](http://www.pariyatti.com/book.cgi?prod_id=404502),* by Nānamoli Thera Kandy: [BPS](dic2-abbrev.htm#BPS), 1964\-98.
>
>
>
>

**[]()Āpo\-dhātu:** Water\-element, macroscopic fluidity, microscopic cohesion; see: [*dhātu*](dic3_d.htm#dhātu)

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "ārammana"
summary = "**[]()Ārammana:** Object. Ther ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Ārammana:** Object. There are six: visible object, sound, odour, taste, body\-contact, mental\-object. The mental\-object *dhammārammana* may be physical or mental, past, present or future, real or imaginary. The 5 sense\-objects belong to the materiality\-group [*rūpa*](dic3_r.htm#rūpa) \- [*khandha*](dic3_k.htm#khandha) see: [*khandha*](dic3_k.htm#khandha). They form the external foundations for the sense\-perceptions, and without them no sense\-perception or sense\-consciousness seeing, hearing, etc. can ever arise. Cf. *[āyatana](#āyatana)* *[paccaya](dic3_p.htm#paccaya).*

**[]()Ārammanupanissaya:** Decisive Support Conditional Relation. see: [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya)



**[]()Āraññikanga:** The training of living in the forest, is one of the ascetic purification\-exercises [*dhutānga*](dic3_d.htm#dhutānga).

``` toml

summary = "**[]()Āruppa:** Formless menta ..."

```

**[]()Āruppa:** Formless mental absorption see: [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna)

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "āsava"
summary = "**[]()Āsava:** lit: fermentati ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Āsava:** lit: fermentations, taints, corruptions, intoxicant biases. There is a list of four as in [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 16, [Pts.M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Pts.M.), [Vibh.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vibh.):  
1: The mental fermentation of sense\-desire [*kāmāsava*](dic3_k.htm#kāmāsava), Ex: 'All is pleasant'  
2: The mental fermentation of desiring existence [*bhavāsava*](dic3_b.htm#bhavāsava), Ex: 'Being is good'  
3: The mental fermentation of wrong views *ditthāsava,* Ex: 'My opinion is best'  
4: The mental fermentation of ignorance *avijjāsava.* Ex: 'Suffering exists not'  
A list of three, omitting the fermentation of views, is possibly older and is more frequent in the Suttas, e.g. in [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 2, [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 9, [D.](dic2-abbrev.htm#D.) 33; [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) III, 59, 67; [A.](dic2-abbrev.htm#A.) VI, 63. In [Vibh.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vibh.) Khuddakavatthu [Vibh.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vibh.) both the 3\-fold and 4\-fold division are mentioned. The fourfold division also occurs under the name of floods [*ogha*](dic3_o.htm#ogha) and yokes [*yoga*](dic3_y.htm#yoga).

Through the [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) of Stream\-Entry, the fermentation of views is destroyed;  
Through the [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) of Non\-Returning, the fermentation of sense\-desire;  
Through the [path](dic3_m.htm#magga) of Arahatship, the fermentations of existence and ignorance.  
[M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 2 shows how to overcome the fermentations, namely, through insight, sense\-control, avoidance, wise use of the necessities of life. For a commentarial exposition, see [Atthasālini](dic2-abbrev.htm#Atthasālini) Tr. I, p. 63f: II, pp. 475ff.

*[khīnāsava](dic3_k.htm#khīnāsava)* = one whose fermentations are eliminated, or one who is fermentation\-free, is a name for the Arahat or Noble One. The state of Arahatship is frequently called [*āsavakkhaya*](dic3_a.htm#āsavakkhaya) the destruction of the fermentations. Suttas concluding with the attainment of Arahatship by the listeners, often end with the words: During this utterance, the minds of the Bhikkhus were freed from the mental fermentations through absence of clinging *anupādāya āsavehi cittāni vimuccimsū’ti.*

``` toml

word = "āsavakkhaya"
summary = "**[]()Āsavakkhaya:** see above ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Āsavakkhaya:** see above.


**[]()Āsevana\-paccaya:** repetition, is one of the 24 conditional relations [*paccaya*](dic3_p.htm#paccaya).

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "āvajjana"
summary = "**[]()Āvajjana:** Directing of ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Āvajjana:** Directing of the mind towards the object, is the first stage in the process of consciousness see: [*viññāna\-kicca*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna-kicca). If an object of the 5 physical senses is observed, it is called 'five\-door directing' *= pañca* *dvārāvajjana,* in the case of a mental object, an idea or mental state then it is called 'mind\-door directing' [*mano*](dic3_m.htm#mano) \- *dvārāvajjana.*

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "āyatana"
summary = "\\*[]()Āyatana:   \\* 1: Spheres ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

\*[]()Āyatana:  
\* 1: Spheres, is a name for the four formless absorptions; see: [*jhāna*](dic3_j.htm#jhāna) 5\-8.  
2: The 12 sources or bases on which depend the mental processes, consist of five physical sense\-organs and consciousness, being the six internal *ajjhattika* sources; and the six objects, the so\-called external *bāhira* sources \- namely:

>
>
>
> * eye, or visual organ and visible object  
>   
>   
>   
> * ear, or auditory organ and sound, or audible object  
>   
>   
>   
> * nose, or olfactory organ and odour, or olfactive object  
>   
>   
>   
> * tongue, or gustatory organ and taste, or gustative object  
>   
>   
>   
> * body, or tactile organ and body\-contact, or tactile object  
>   
>   
>   
> * mind\-base, or consciousness and idea or mental\-object  
>   *manāyatana dhammāyatana*
>   
>   
>
>
>
>

By the visual organ *[cakkhāyatana](dic3_c.htm#cakkhāyatana)* is meant the sensitive part of the eye [*cakkhu*](dic3_c.htm#cakkhu) \- *pasāda* (retina) built up of the four elements… responding to sense\-stimuli *sa* \- *ppatigha.* [Vibh.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vibh.) II. Similar is the explanation of the four remaining physical sense\-organs.

The source\-of\-mind [*manāyatana*](dic3_m.htm#manāyatana) is a collective term for all consciousness whatsoever, and should therefore not be confounded with the mental\-element [*mano\-dhātu*](dic3_m.htm#mano-dhātu) see: [*dhātu*](dic3_d.htm#dhātu) II, 16, which latter performs only the functions of directing [*āvajjana*](dic3_a.htm#āvajjana) attention to the sense\-object, and of receiving *[sampaticchana](dic3_s.htm#sampaticchana-citta)* the data of the sense\-object. On the functions of the mind, see: [*viññāna\-kicca*](dic3_v.htm#viññāna-kicca)

The visible object [*rūpāyatana*](dic3_r.htm#rūpāyatana) is described in [Vibh.](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vibh.) II as that phenomenon which is built up of the four primary elements and appears as color and form. What is seen by\-visual perception, i.e. by visual\-consciousness [*cakkhu\-viññāna*](dic3_c.htm#cakkhu-viññāna) are only colors and different intensities of light, but not three dimensional bodily things, which are interpretations.

The thinkable mental\-object\-source [*dhammāyatana*](dic3_d.htm#dhammāyatana) is identical with 'mental\-object\-element' [*dhamma\-dhātu*](dic3_d.htm#dhamma-dhātu), [*dhātu*](dic3_d.htm#dhātu) II\-17 and *dhammārammana* see: [*ārammana*](dic3_a.htm#ārammana). It may be physical or mental, past, present or future, real or imaginary.

The 5 physical sense\-organs are also called abilities [*indriya*](dic3_i.htm#indriya), and of these abilities it is said in [M.](dic2-abbrev.htm#M.) 43: Each of the five abilities owns a different domain, and none of them partakes of the domain of another one;… they have mind as their support… are conditioned by mental vitality (neural metabolic activity).

The 12 sense\-source are fully discussed in [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XV. In Yam III see: [Guide](dic2-abbrev.htm#Guide), p 98f. are  
the 12 terms are subjected to a logical investigation The six internal bases form the 5th link of dependent origination [*paticca* \- *samuppāda*](dic3_p.htm#paticcasamuppāda) 5.

``` toml
dict_label = "Nyana"
word = "āyūhana"
summary = "**[]()Āyūhana:** K ammic accum ..."
grammar = ""
inflections = []
```

**[]()Āyūhana:** K ammic accumulation, is a name used in the commentarial literature for the advantageous and disadvantageous intentional activities kamma or kammic\-constructions [*sankhāra*](dic3_s.htm#sankhāra) (see: [*paticca* \- *samuppāda*](dic3_p.htm#paticcasamuppāda) 2), being the causes of future rebirth. Accumulation, is a name for the past kammic\-constructions, and signifies those intentions *[cetanā](dic3_c.htm#cetanā),* which arised at the performance of a kamma, first while thinking 'I will give food', and then while actually giving the food or any other object. The intention, however, at the time when one is handing the food over to the recipient is called kamma\-making or kamma\-becoming *[kamma\-bhava](dic3_k.htm#kamma-bhava)* see. [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XVII, IX, X. Or, the intentions during the first six impulse\-moments [*javana*](dic3_j.htm#javana) depending on one and the same state of directing [*āvajjana*](dic3_a.htm#āvajjana) (see. *[viññāna\-kicca](dic3_v.htm#viññāna-kicca)* ), these are called the kammic\-constructions, whilst the 7th impulse moment is called the kamma\-making [*kamma\-bhava*](dic3_k.htm#kamma-bhava). Or, each moment of intention is called kamma\-making and the accumulation connected with it, kamma\-construction. [Vis.M](dic2-abbrev.htm#Vis.M.) XVII. Cf. [*paticca* \- *samuppāda*](dic3_p.htm#paticcasamuppāda) 2, 10 \- [App.](dic4_append.htm#āyūhana)
